Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When the entire illness of peritoneum is due to cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or thirst, and the disease is chronic, then perform two cauteries on the lower abdomen in visible areas; and another cautery between the chest and one of the breasts; and use the "clavicle" type of cautery, as mentioned earlier.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if necessary, apply cautery to the entire area of the one called "poins," of which the form is previously given in the treatment for ear disease; and let the poins be up to thirty or around it.[Note: The exact meaning of "poins" is unclear without additional context, but it likely refers to a specific type of cautery tool or technique. I have translated it as "poins" to retain the original term.]
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After the treatment, put back in place according to what is said before, and let the cautery be three fingers in size according to this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And that is why cauteries are lighter, because you make three of them at one stroke.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, have the patient recline on his back and side; then lift the heart that is within the chest with the tips of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two nerves such as this, here is its form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the heart until it penetrates to the ribs, and the figure of the cautery would come together as four cauteries; and for this reason, the cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, so that the figures of cauterization are six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a tent and here is the shape of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted on this one nerve so that there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, place the punctured cautery that has been crushed with oil on it; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is fully healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated on top, then little happens, in that case, do cautery on the thick part of the collarbone with a small cautery or apply many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When cold and moisture come to the stomach, causing an imbalance in its constitution and producing excessive amounts of phlegm that do not respond to usual treatments, then the patient should be positioned on their back with legs and arms extended.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 Of this later, I make three fire cauteries below the shoulder blade of the back, of the quantity of one finger, with the entire cautery nail, and two cauteries outside the two ribs, so that the shape of the cauteries is at three angles, and have such space between one and the other that they will not be joined together when they are thrown out for corruption; and let the cauteries be so deep that they penetrate both parts of the flesh, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without deviation:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and one who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and pressing slightly on the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you wish to apply; then cauterize it with the entire cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the care of the wound that we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 As for pain in the liver due to cold and moisture, and swelling, which causes it to be displaced from its natural state due to excess; and the patient is not relieved by the treatments we have mentioned earlier, then they should pay attention to their diet; and place three cautery marks according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondria (the region below the ribcage), where the edge of the ribs are; and leave a space between each cautery equal to the width of a finger; and let the cauteries be long and not too narrow; and only burn half the thickness of the skin; and let the patient be in an upright position, if they can, and if not, then let them lie down with their legs extended and arms raised; and this is the method.
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with the scalpel, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and take care not to burn the entire heart, for you would make the whole body dry out; and let it not boil, for the heart is very delicate in that regard, and be aware of this.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels not too severe pain; and if it is in the capsule, the pain is intense.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And when this treatment should be performed by the doctors, it is necessary that the patient lies on his back; and then bind in place the location where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a rod, of which this is the method:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And cauterize with the cautery until the core is burnt, and bring it up to boil, until all pus is expelled; after that, treat it with wound care until it is healed; and it is not appropriate for anyone other than those who have studied medicine for a long time to use this cautery, through whom many of these illnesses have been cured at times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can boldly work, and yet it seems to me that moving is better than leaving it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy using aristolochia roots, and in this way: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your finger; and moisten it in oil and hold it over the fire and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries a little lower in the part that is below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth rib, declining slightly behind; and one in the middle of the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two at the sides of the breast outside the cautery which is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather make it open as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some ancient said that certain people use the fire cautery resembling a razor, heating and placing it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and if this is done correctly, the pain will disappear, just as we have mentioned in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, there is fear that the patient may die immediately or a fistula may form which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse (or mice)
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse (or mice) in those that I have mentioned in the methods of treatment, and it does not help at all, then there are three types of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 Of which one way is that you make three or four cauteries, aligning them according to the length of the vein, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we mentioned before; and do not press your hand too hard on the entire cautery, let the patient be lying on their back; and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery that has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the rib cage which is next to the vein, where the patient's ribs come towards the left side, and let the lifting of the ribcage be according to the height of the ribcage, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After put in the two nerves inflamed until the core is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and so there will be four [nerves] injured. And if you wish, cauterize all of it with the entire cautery on three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After the treatment when it has cast off gangrene for a long time, and it is worth moving that which was said in other treatments.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 The cautery is not suitable for a hydroptic patient, except for the method called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When you treat it according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help at all, then you must make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the bladder, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the nipple; and let the cauteries be close to the thickness of the core.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery on to ripen the rottenness for a long time, and do not stop caring for the patient after the cautery; and if sanation is hurried, both intentions will come together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the claw that we have shown before; and the one for the back should be olive-shaped, as it is described earlier.[IT] Li cauteres de feu ne doivent estre mout granz, ainz soient plus menu et longues, por ce que li grant cautere desfigure le cors del malaide.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swollen feet

de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy part which is called "thigh"

And if necessary, perform more; and if they know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then make a knife-like or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cauter on for too long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause more harm and contraction to the patient.

Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then it will be very cool and is used in various medical operations and in cauterizing other limbs because it performs a similar function as fire, and it also has other medicines that are used to cauterize inflammation, such as terebinth and anacardic acid and lime with soap, all mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure whereby a man was cured of the pain of a hernia and sciatic pain, and he praised it highly, saying that no other cure was done, and that he was healed in one go when this cure was performed, and he had bathed as instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says in this manner to take fresh and dry litharge (lead oxide), grind it well with a little fat, and apply it to the hernia and on the thigh and leg where the pain resides, and bind it; and leave it on for three hours, and by the amount that the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then have them enter the bath until their body is slightly aroused, and have them enter the bed, and the pain will go away completely and they will be healed.[printk(f"{translation}")]
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use a fire cautery of such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of humors.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Afterwards, take dry goat's dung and heat it over the fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the wool, leaving it until it becomes extinguished; and do this again and do not stop doing so until you think by sense that it reaches the swelling, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "goat's dung cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling, or impact, or from excessive evacuation, or from the spreading of cold matter, no form of cautery is effective except for that which results from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or similar treatments, three lines be signed with ink on the back, in the area where the pain is located, and on each line there should be five cauterizations or more depending on the strength and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and let the cauterizations be made using the type of cautery called "poins"; and if you wish, perform three or four cauterizations with a clavile moien cautery of this shape:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have stiffness in their limbs when they get up and fear; and you will find in the spine at the base of the back, and appearing above the other spines, a swelling.[LOLTYPE: ]
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this, and wish to cure it, cauterize with the cautery of this shape.[LOLTYPE: ](https://i.imgur.com/Rh1J5UA.png)Here is an image of the type of cautery referred to in the text. It is a pointed cautery that was commonly used in medieval medicine for a variety of treatments, including cauterization of wounds and abscesses. The shape of the cautery would have been created by heating a piece of iron until it was red-hot and then using it to burn or seal the skin. In this case, the text specifies that the cautery should be used to treat a swelling found at the base of the spine in children. Cauterization with a hot iron would have been a painful procedure, but it was believed to have healing properties by sealing wounds and preventing infection. The use of cautery in medieval medicine has largely been replaced by modern surgical techniques, but it is still used in some cases today, such as for the treatment of certain types of cancer.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 That the fire cautery affects each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the fire cautery, making two or three lines and keeping the points close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 Afterwards, treat the area until it is healed as we have said, and be careful not to apply the cautery to gout that is in a nerve spasm.[](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZMh2_rk7JxU)
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to moisture that has spread throughout the body, and when pain occurs in the feet, which is called "gout" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it can be cured by cauterization in the following manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary to cauterize on the face of the foot, use the entire fire cautery so that it is called "touch" (meaning a single point).
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pains reach down to the knees and other joints, which happens frequently, cauterize on each knee three or four times on each side with the entire olive-shaped fire cautery; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand over it for longer than it takes for the surface of the skin to be burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend down to the knee and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines long; and if there is no more pain, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the wrists or down to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and give them medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you take good care of them and purge the phlegm, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rottenness of the syphilis
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an abscess comes to a head and the intestines descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see to cure it, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that empty the belly so that the feces descend from their belly; after make them sit on their back between your hands, and instruct them to hold their belly in until the abscess has receded, and massage it with your hands, and direct steam from beneath the abscess onto the bone of the hip, and in such a way that it forms half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: [shape description follows]
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 as long as it is white and excreting pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then return the bowels to their place; and the assistant places his hand so that they do not move back; and work well the thighs for the patient, and put a cushion and a servant beneath the thighs, and another on the stomach who holds the hands; then place the cautery on the sign with your entire hand, and hold it straight and steady until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again until you come to the bone; and carefully watch that the bowels do not protrude when you apply the cautery; so that you do not burn him; and so that through this the patient does not die, or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And it is necessary that the cautery for children be fine, according to the measure of eggs, and for adults also as large according to their measure; after three days cure the wound of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; after curing other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left long enough so that the boils do not come out when he moves to get up from bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, let him use a well-made belt and wear it for another forty days; and have good rest, do not exert himself too much and be careful with overconsumption of drinks and food, and loud talking; and when he follows this instruction, he will be fully healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Here is the translation for the given Old French text:
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, perform the fire cautery of the round cautery according to its size, and let a third of the belly be burnt; then cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the three-angled cautery in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the location of the rupture and make a line across its width above it, and another below it, and place your hand in the middle of the entire cauterizing iron.[Read More](https://masterofcode.medium.com/)
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and sharper.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes to any member, either from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical care is of no use, then it should be cauterized with the cautery known as "pointed", and let the cautery be in accordance to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and strength, and its location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, start another cautery on top of it, for it is often the case that it must change to the member that is close by, therefore you should continue with the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The measles are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 If you wish to cauterize the eyes, take care if the illness is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and if it does not subside or remain, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then perform two caureties on the head: one at the forehead, and the other toward the front at the end of the hairline; and two above the ears, and one behind at the back of the skull; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the blisters come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the spot according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the illness is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the thighs of the hips, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollow of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are at the rear pressing against the spine, so as not to burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one another on the bone of the stomach, and one another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more I do with fire cautery, the more help I provide, and it benefits the sick; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as a healthy person does, because the body is already entirely corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the fire cautery should be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Afterwards, sprinkle the wound with barley flour and honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When inflammation comes upon any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but is not healed, then cauterize the limb according to its size; and let the cauter be slightly into the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes a fire cautery is done on the hand, foot, and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and in this way the swelling is removed; but no one should intervene if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of ulcers/sores
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has awakened, and the means of medicine are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery somewhat deeply, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and one part each of swine's blood and pigeon's blood; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the curing of chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a chancre first appears and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a fire cautery that forms a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 And yet the experts say that one should also perform cauterization in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem right to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen before; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized all around with the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot mature/ripen
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in killing, either due to the superfluity it causes or the water of the sick person when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; leave it like that afterwards.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 as it will hurry to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you want to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery until it is red-hot, as shown in the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that illness called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the heart, and make such cauteries that the patient feels them from outside in such a way that the course of the gangrene is alleviated.[Note: The word "porriture" refers to decomposition or rotting of flesh.]
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the care until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the healing by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another kind of illness exists which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing but a consumption of the limb, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate the application of a hot cautery, then heat the cautery rod slowly and gradually, according to where the illness is located; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, leaving nothing behind, so that all of what is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and apply to the cauterized areas crushed herbs with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, as well as all of the corruption.[.](Note: in medieval medical texts, "broiet" often refers to crushed or powdered herbs applied as a poultice)
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the treatment of ointments causing flesh to grow.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if you see that healthy flesh has not grown after three days, that is good; and if not, then reapply the cautery to the remaining areas of corrupt flesh.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this inflammation has sometimes been cured with medicinal liquids in place of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is of greater help. I have already mentioned the cure for inflammation using medicinal liquids in the previous section: take what you need when necessary.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of fungi that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 It often happens that in the feet there arises a disease called "clos" in our language, and it is a large abscess that wounds the foot.[Note: The word "clos" in Old French can mean "swelling, ulcer". Here, it seems to refer to an ingrown toenail or similar condition causing swelling and pain in the toe/foot area.]
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries for this disease are of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 The cautery of fire is: heat the cauterizing iron as if it were a roof tile pen, and make it of good metal, of a size that can touch the nail from all sides, with fine edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and hold your hand all around the nail until you reach the base of the nail; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to putrefy; then make a plaster of crushed mallows with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure the wound by applying ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if they are swollen due to fluid in the body, which happens frequently in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery. Here's how: take an iron or copper rod, or a chicken wing bone, and place it on the nail and attach garlic, that is, powdered verrucae; then place the rod so that it surrounds completely, then add some hot water, and hold your hand firmly and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the rod comes into contact with the base of the nail, allowing the hot water to penetrate deep to the root. Let the patient endure the biting pain of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as is, and it will fall out along with its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Do one after the other, so that you cauterize all those in the body, then cure the inflammations that cause flesh to grow.
li cure dou trembler	the care of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from coldness of nerves, or quartan fever or otherwise, you should make for them four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery or plaster at the navel, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery; then the trembling will subside, and their recovery from the cold disease will be hastened.
des pustules puans	fetid pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes it happens that the body appears covered in weak spots or putrid pustules, which come from thick corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 When they first appear, you should apply a cautery to each pustule: use a slender probe made of myrtle wood, with the tip heated in fire, or a long root of aristolochia, or use a round-shaped cautery.[Google Translate](https://translate.google.com/#auto/en/si%20covient%20au%20premier%20quant%20el%C3%ABs%20apperent%20que%20on%20faice%20cautere%20sus%20chescun%20chief%20de%20la%20pustule%3A%20un%20cautere%20subtil%20de%20fust%20de%20mirte%2C%20de%20coi%20li%20pointe%20soit%20emprise%20au%20feu%2C%20ou%20de%20racine%20de%20aristologe%20longe%2C%20ou%20au%20cautere%20lenticulaire.)
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the superfluidities from which they come are broken off, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut or severed.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are large flows of blood from the artery that is cut by the wound, or by the incision of the abscess, or by the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drips from it; then heat various olive-shaped cauters, both small and large, until they are all red; then apply one, whether large or small, according to the wound and the location where the artery is located, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it starts to bleed again when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cauter is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauters that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this until the bleeding has stopped; and make sure that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when there is a cut in the artery, it cannot be easily stopped if the artery is large, except by one of the four methods we have mentioned: using cautery, or extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with bandages, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and make sure it is bound and held in place appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will treat tight constriction with bandages or placing hot things on it, or similar things, it will not help much.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have any remedy or medicine, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and pull it tight until it is stretched over the wound and the vein; and they should not move it, but moisten it frequently with very cold water until the blood congeals and swells and becomes sealed; and prepare what is needed for cauteries and medicines in advance.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases for which it is necessary to use cautery with fire or hot medicine, and we have described the instruments and methods of cauterization; and I have put this chapter about the head down to the feet, and in this chapter I will proceed in the same manner so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is appropriate, dear friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you not to undertake a foolish thing.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many kinds of people come to be healed.[ ](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/Et+je+vos+amoneste+que+vos+n%E2%80%99entreprenez+folie.Car+mout+de+manieres+de+gens+vienent+en+cures.)
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 Those who are so afflicted by their illness that they would easily die from the violence of their disease and the severity of their suffering belong to this category; and one should be afraid of them.[ ](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/Et+je+vos+amoneste+que+vos+n%E2%80%99entreprenez+folie.Car+mout+de+manieres+de+gens+vienent+en+cures.si+vienent+de+telz+qui+s%E2%80%99a%C3%AFrent+si+avec+lor+maladie+qu%E2%80%99il+muerent+legierement+por+la+forsenerie+qu%E2%80%99il+truve+de+sa+maladie.+et+de+ces+doit+on+avoir+paor.)
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And of these there are some who give you their word and say: "wait, I am healed"; and the illness is contemptuous. (meaning: Some patients will tell you they are healed, but they are still sick)
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not at all appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but put more effort into your honor than into your greed, and do not rashly but wisely open up those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain benefit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients for their health to be restored; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire of the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And I have organized this chapter by speaking of chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have explained from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a swollen head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes very often to children when they are being born, and when the birth passage squeezes the child's head too hard; and sometimes it happens for no known reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death hastened; and for this reason, it seems better to me to abandon the work in such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child where the head was full of water, and the skull thickened each day to the point that it could no longer support it; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture is collected under the bone on the temple, between the brain and the bone; and the procedure is such if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the middle of the head a wide opening; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture can flow out; and here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the corners of the mouth open on both sides, and the water jumps out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not respond, then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, remove all the moisture (pus) out.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 After tighten the wounds of cloth and powders, and put wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then loosen it, and cure the wound with tenting and ointments, and also keep the head bound up, and give dry food to the patient in small amounts of moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is to look where the swelling of the abscess is prominent and where the water has gathered; for it can be in front, behind, to the right, or to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut there then where the abscess is prominent and where the water has gathered, and make an incision according to your ability; and take care not to cut the artery; and if blood comes out in a flood, so that the patient dies from bleeding and evacuation of pus.
de reume	It seems like you have provided a single word "de reume" which is not a complete sentence. I'm assuming you would like to know its translation in English? If yes, then "de reume" can be translated as "of rheum" or "of watery discharge".
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a person gets a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the lungs, and the illness is chronic, and medical treatment does not help at all, then the last resort cure is the fire cautery, where they will burn two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Therefore, when you cover the eyes, it is necessary for the patient to turn his head back; then rub the area around the eye with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then have the patient strain his neck against the cloth; then look where the vein bulges, and the place on both sides of the ears is swollen and not sunken; then make an incision in those places with a lancet sharpened to half its original size, so that the cut reaches the bone, and this should be done across the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see an artery, place the lancet underneath it and cut above it, making two incisions crosswise like a pair of dice.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will spout out continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery does not open to feeling, you should measure the quantity of three fingers' space, then make an incision and cut down to the bone; and that amount of blood which must come out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can tolerate and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if pus remains on the surface of the syphac, cut it away so that no abscess comes, then close the wound and bind it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	de grain(s), and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can withstand, and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if pus remains on the bone point of the syphac, cut it out so that no abscess comes, then tighten the wound and bind it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old grain (headache) and acute catarrh come, from moisture of tears and heat in the temples, and swelling of the forehead and madness of the old age and similar things, and it is treated with various medical cures without success, then we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is as follows: the patient should shave the hairs from their temples, and pay attention to the artery which can be felt in the temple, for it is easily discernible due to its pulsation, and is not very noticeable except in some men who are too cold; and if it is not noticeable, then have the patient strain their neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and apply hot water to the area until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take a spatula of this shape (here the text includes a description of the shape).
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then lightly skin the leather until you reach the artery, then pull it up with forceps, and separate it well from the membranes beneath it in each part; and if the artery is fine, turn it with the point of the probe, then cut that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 For if it is not cut, the blood will not leave entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw blood from the six holes until three; and if the arteries are large, then you must tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk, so that gangrene does not set in before the wound is healed and proper bleeding occurs; then cut away the excess that is between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize the remaining part with a scalpel cautery up to the bone until the holes are cauterized; and this is the more difficult task, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery stops moisture: therefore it is of greater help for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	In which case, for the extraction of arteries, one must fill the wound with old cotton and apply well-made bandages; and when they are removed, cure it with dry medicines that promote healing and bandages until it is healed; and if an artery is cut as you work, then quickly cover it with a cautery or use vitriol in the wound and press on it to stop the bleeding; and if you don't have this available, place your finger on the wound until the blood clots, and apply cold water to the area until the bleeding stops, and press as needed. And the more difficult and lighter method for extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein with a two-sided cutting cautery, but make sure that the blade is thick enough to maintain its heat for longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a gap of the width of a finger between the two knives, and when you have marked the two places, place your hot iron upon them until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be far apart because this cautery is not welded together in its entirety; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	Of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears descend from the veins which are above the temple of the head and no medicine helps, and you see the face of the patient redden, and feel a pulsation on the forehead like a tremor; and if the eyelids are tight and moist so that the paper has fallen off, and the paper is heated up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And the ancients called it "cure contused", and it consists of making three incisions on the forehead of the patient who has this illness, so that they have hair on their forehead. The first incision should be in the middle of the forehead, from the beginning to the end, and the other two should be above the eyebrows. Be careful not to cut the arteries which are located above the eyebrows. Keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones. Each wound should be the width of three fingers joined together. Prepare a piece of sponge and plenty of bandages to clean the blood, then place the styptic agent (which is in the form of) on both sides. Here is its composition:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is made above the temple to the second incision; and scrape off all the flesh that is between the two cuts, right up to the sutures on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this mixture.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	insert into the first cut the instrument called "cultellaria", which is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, with the following form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And place the cutting edge towards the fleshy part of the ribcage near the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and push until it comes to the middle split. (My translation)
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to where the heart is visible, and then do the same in the middle split to the other side; and then bleed equally, and press the area for bloodletting; then place a piece of old cotton in each split, and put wet bandages on it with wine and oil and vinegar, and make sure no abscess comes there; and on the third day loosen the binding, and apply a lot of cold water, then treat with basilicon ointment and rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
