dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone is accustomed to getting a catarrh, and you see their eyes sunken and small, with weakened vision and burning paper; and their hair falls out, and they have deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that those substances and catarrh do not come out but from many veins, and the cure for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And instruct the patient to bend his forehead, then make a big slit between the eyebrows, and another one an inch wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 Begin at the slit of the left temple and continue to the right temple, cutting down to the bone; keep your hand away from the temple nerves that move when eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the slit and place a piece of old cotton and linen cloth; then bind damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, but be careful to avoid causing a hot abscess; when it is removed, rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying agents that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make it into an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	for stopping up ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains or animals, or mineral fragments such as iron; or seeds, such as lice, beans, peas; or fluids such as water and mucus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear a stone or any other thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, then place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, distill a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then attempt extraction; and make them sneeze with a powder, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and hold the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 This cure often brings forth the stone; and if it does not come out, attempt extraction with subtle forceps, of which this is the form: [The text goes on to describe the shape and size of the forceps, but it's a bit difficult to translate precisely without seeing the original illustration or description.]
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, then perform an extraction using a thin probe of double-refined silver; and if it does not come out with this, then make a small tube of tin and insert the end into the ear canal, and stop up what is around the tube with soft wax so that no air can enter with the tube; then pull it out forcefully, for often it will come out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take birdlime and put some on an instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and place a piece of cotton around it; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with any of the things that we have mentioned, then quickly make an incision in the ear so that pus and hardened matter do not form; and the manner of making the incision is as follows: first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein and draw blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards; and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty or fleshy part; and make the incision like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck on it with your mouth; treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and becomes swollen, perform evacuation; and if it cannot come out, apply a thin spatula in this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and treat the incision of that boil.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this when you think that the boil is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then carefully extract it with tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Therefore, in water that falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing of condiments first and widen the ear with soft cotton.[Note: "condiments" here likely refers to substances used to induce sneezing as a way to clear the ear.]
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And lie on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out by itself, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If not, take many small and light pebbles, heat them slightly by the fire, and place one or two of them in the patient's ear where the water is, and lie on your side. Then strike the stone in the ear with another pebble; and do not stop doing this pebble after pebble until all the water comes out and jumps out completely. And if you want, take a reed, and put one end of it in the ear, and light the other end on fire until the inner part of the reed is burned; then repeat this with another piece of reed until all the water comes out, as we have said with the pebbles.[Note: "reed" here likely refers to a hollow plant stem that can be used as a tube for insertion into the ear.]
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is small-bodied, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is large-bodied and can be felt, then apply extraction with pincers, for this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms, then pull them out with fine tweezers, and if you don't see any, then take a probe of the kind described here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And should be tight below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And insert the thinnest end of the earwax probe according to the patient's discomfort, then thoroughly draw out all the wax; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not obey by coming out, stop up around the wax with cotton as I said in the previous instruction; and if they do not come out as we have described, administer the distillations that the ancients have proven to work in removing worms, which you can find in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument. Here is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or brass, narrow below with a small hole, and wide at the top for distilling; and for pressing the distillation inside, there should be a well-made brass instrument for this purpose, and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you choose of your medicines into the probe, and place the probe in the ear; then insert the scraper all the way in with the cotton, and press gently until the oil is distilled or reaches the ear canal; and let the patient feel it inside, and the distillation should be a small flask heated by fire so that it can be distilled into the ear; and make sure it's not too cold, because the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	for stopping up ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have an opening in the ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to blockage from wound or pus inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small hole instead of the opening, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that goes deep and cannot be seen is of difficult healing in many cases. And for the one that can be seen, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; look inside: if you see any blockage, work on it immediately using this method:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make the tool sharp and blunt at both ends so that it does not injure the ear; if the blockage is from pus or flesh in the ear, hold it with delicate pincers, and remove it gently until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if pus is deep in the ear, take a thin, light razor, heat it slightly by fire, then put it in the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you notice pus of which the patient feels discomfort in hearing, make a small incision, but be careful not to injure the ear's nerves; then insert into the ear a wick according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder on top of vitriol broken; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw the tent and apply another tent soaked in cerate which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	The meaning of "de la char des papieres" is unclear without additional context. However, one possible interpretation could be "from the pulp of paper".
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that comes in paper when the eyes are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tongs and forceps, and cut off a piece of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on the place.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is not corrected, then cauterize it with a subtle circular cautery, and after the incision, the cauterizer should move; and many times they heal, when some things remain of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return at all.
de la gresle	Of the hail.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Many times there come from the eyelids small things that resemble grains in their shape and hardness, and for this reason, this illness is called "hail"; it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: observe if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is an easy thing to know; then make an incision of appropriate size, then carefully scrape from each part, then take it with forceps and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 if you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, suture it with a stitch and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will soon restore it and help heal the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn over the skin and extend the hail with tweezers and cut it and press it from one side and the other; and if the skin is separated by incision, it does not matter; and when the hail is removed, rinse the eye with salty water and cure the wound of whatever causes inflammation until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is an ointment that is applied to paper and placed on (the eyelids of) children more often than others, and it greatly harms their eyes; and they get mucus in the mornings, and cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they lie with their faces downward and sleep on it, and their papers beneath their eyelids become moist and swollen and the appearance of exinach is evident in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the end of the bone move apart.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the procedure is as follows: the patient places their head over your sanctioned area; then take a linen cloth and fashion a tent in the shape of a circle, corresponding to the amount of exinach present in each part, and place it on top of them. Then press with your fingers from both sides so that the exinach is gathered into the circle. Next, make an incision in the middle of the moisture using a small knife, and do not make it any larger than the wound made during venesection; then cut through the skin until you reach the exinach. And in multiple ways, the exinach will come out of the incision, appearing as a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it as one piece of cloth between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and make sure not to press too hard on the incision, so that you do not reach the entire small knife all the way up to the eye, causing it to bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not appear at the beginning of the cut, slightly increase the cut lengthwise until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then wet bandages in oil and water, and place them on the wound, and bind it with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if there are such people who crush ice and apply it to corrupt the moisture that has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if a hot abscess comes to the joint, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.[Note: I translated "emplaustres" as "plasters" because they were often used in medieval medicine for various purposes including healing wounds and abscesses. However, depending on the context, they could also be translated as "poultices" or "compresses".]
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of papyrus or parchment (based on context)
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on papyrus or parchment that are not natural and have aged, they harm the eyes and cause various illnesses such as tears and swelling of the papyrus/parchment and inflammation, to the point where it causes the destruction of the eyes. And there are four ways to cure this: either through cautery with fire or through a water-based medicine, according to what is before the chapter on cautery. It can be done through incision and suturing or by using leeches, depending on what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, insert a needle with a thread at one end; and let this be beside the edge of the paper where the hairs grow near the hairs, and pull the thread over the entire paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision beneath the paper, beneath the adjacent hairs, to the full width, from the large tear duct to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place underneath the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then lay on the paper a figure of a bandage, such as a myrtle leaf, and yet it is necessary that the figure be in accordance with the quantity you wish to raise the paper which is determined.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if some need to have a large amount of paper applied according to how soft the paper is; then apply ointment to the entire area along the two lines you have designated, starting from the large tear down to the small one. Make one of the cuts close to the natural hairs, about the size of a root, then insert the probe into one of the two angles of the wound and cut it open. Then stitch the two sides together with a needle and fine thread, wipe away the blood, and use tweezers to remove any excess threads that are sticking to anything; or if not, don't worry about it, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days. Then heal the wound without dry or constricting materials because the paper will swell when it comes into contact with the wound, bringing the two sides together (as the ancients said), and this is a painless procedure. There is also another method: you can shape the paper like a myrtle leaf with three slits along its edges as we have described earlier.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what protrudes with small force equally according to the form that is below:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you do not have the power to hold the pincers, and the thing is not even, take a needle with a thread, and place it in the middle of the wound; and place another thread next to the large notch, and the second thread next to the small one, and align the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have told; then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar calming ointments; and it sometimes happens that the hairs of the skin turn white: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitches in one and the other are more refined.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of veins is as follows: and it is that you turn the skin and make an incision according to what I have said, and then make two sutures with skill, and two thin threads as long as the skin and the width of the scalpel is; and cut the two corners from two sides where you hold the threads; then bring one and the other together gently on top of the paper of the eye, and pull the two sutures firmly from both sides; and leave it like that for a few days, and the skin that was stretched will die and turn black and rot until it falls off.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it delays, strike it with force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is knitted together, and the paper is removed, and the hairs will no longer prickle; and this is the shape of the two sinews that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work is as follows: take a thin needle and thread a soft and fine strand of silk; then bring the edges together and tie them delicately, and let the length of the threads be a palm in length; then place another fine strand of silken thread in the groove and delicately tie the ends of the thread; then place the patient's head in your lap; and be in a sunny spot so that the work is well-lit, for it is delicate and fine work; then insert the needle into the entire groove at the root of the hair; quickly make it penetrate the paper, as you pull it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the groove, and insert the pulled-out hairs into the groove, if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out at the entire groove in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the groove is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will draw the groove underneath all the thread that you have placed in it, until the groove comes out of the opening and you see it with your eye; then you will draw the groove and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair dries in its place and new growth appears; and if the hairs are small, then attach one long hair from the natural hair, and lift it up with that or let it be, until it is lengthened and then you lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of eye rot.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "alecrati" or the rottenness comes to the eye, it is of two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from surgery or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the method of the treatment for it is that you split this suture, and separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside, and bind it until it is healed; and you should not at all use drying or constricting agents in its cure.[`](https://llm.library.wisc.edu/cgi-bin/Pwebrecon.cgi?v=1.0&DB=local&CC=*french+old&Search_Arg=Et+avient+par+soudement+de+plaie%2C+ou+de+tailleure+ou+de+cautere%2C+et+par+semblans+choses.&Search_Code=GSS&CNT=50&PID=9lFHvZ1eLxJQKzGyZfJrVbRd4qZp&SD=15)
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but work with softening agents, such as fenugreek; and cook the juice of lettuce or chicory and flaxseed, and heat up ointments of dyaquilon in one of the oils, and wrap it in a compress, and cure with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the key to your treatment is to take care that it does not heal in the same shape as it was before; and these operations that we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return to its former state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness that is underneath, truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wound and fissure and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you take a needle, with two threads, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear to the right, so that the threads come in two parts of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cover it with a space of one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the form of the paper returns as it should, it is good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits along the edge inside the paper; and let the corners of the two splits be the two angles of the incision you have made, and make them so that when they are assembled, the form is like the shape of a letter called "Greek I"; then remove that flesh, according to the amount that its edges are jagged beneath, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with what we have said of soothing medicines and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a split, stitch, or cautery, you must make an incision, cutting a clean split under the hairs of the paper, as has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage as I have mentioned; and the work should be done according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters must prepare means to the best of their ability to make the form return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is required of labor and various instruments.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this bonding happens to many people in such a way that the paper is bonded to the white of the eye, and they cannot move or perform their natural tasks, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, as much as you cut what is hardened on the thin membrane, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient can endure that the membrane does not cut the eye too much; and let your incision, from which you flay this assembly, be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and let this entire assembly be healed, and sometimes put salty water in the eye, and remove it with clear water and collyrium; then place a linen bandage between the paper and the eye, and place wool moistened in egg yolk on the eye; and after three days use collyrium and other drying things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the toe of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the toe has two forms: it is nerve-like and similar to a hard pimple, and another which is not at all nerve-like, but is similar to congealed white moisture, which when touched with iron and one attempts to pinch it, cannot be; and one and the other form begins near the outer corner of the eye, and grows little by little until it covers the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: let the patient place their head in your healthy hand, then open their eyes; lift the paper with your other hand, then curl the toe using small forceps, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle and put a horsehair, cow hair, or ox hair through it along with strong thread; double the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the toe, piercing it completely with the needle, and bind the toe with one thread and stretch it upwards; then skin the entire side of the toe that follows the eyelid and the fatty tissue to the hair using a sharp knife, leaving the natural skin or eyelid, so that the body's tears do not come out through the incision as usual; and sometimes the toe extends only to the knuckle and to the thread, as we have said; then skin off all the soft fatty tissue from which the following form is made:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the fleshy skin and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision place a little bit of crushed salt into the eye, as well as a collyrium made from litharge (lead monoxide), and leave it in until the next day; then cure it with whatever is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sensitive, and you can't insert the needle, and the forceps can't enter, this similarity of a nail is often cured with medicines; and it grows back as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, let the patient's eye watch, and take the spatula, thin and slightly sharpened, according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail carefully, and if you see that it does not thin out and the edges come together, then distill into the eye from your mouth a collyrium made of litharge and red kohl and oil, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes it in the eye, such as an abscess, then leave it alone, and cure the hot abscess first until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.[*](footnote-1)
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid harms the eye with great injury, then suspend it with a thread and cut away some but not all of it, so that tears can still reach; then instill in the eye a red collyrium made of litharge.[*](footnote-1)
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 The eyes of some men are sometimes born with a red scar, covering the pupil and turning it towards the whites, appearing like a rosy ballista; and the procedure is that the patient places his head onto your support, then you open his eyes, and pull all that skin towards the eyelashes using tweezers, holding it with force; then cut the first skin, and continue cutting to the very end using a razor, making sure not to wound the eye during the procedure; and let the incision be done with the spatula that I mentioned in the incision of the nail and small swellings from which one removes pus, as shown in the following form after this chapter; and when the incision is completed and all skin is removed, apply eye ointment made of boiled rose water or you distill red bile and similar corrosive medicines, and place cotton with egg white yolk on top of the eye, ensuring it is secured from hot abscess; and if anything remains, and the blood flow overcomes it, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye and cure the abscess with calming hot abscess remedies; then return to your work until it is healed, and do so for every skin layer attached to the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is important to lighten the treatment for each weak eye according to its natural disposition and accidental causes through surgery; and never force your hand in any of these procedures until you see that this part can withstand the treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Certain are red veins that are located above the eye and impede its proper functioning, causing it to weaken every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary, firstly, that you look to see if the eye, in which the swelling is, is outside [its socket], and there is no other illness but the swelling; then the eye in such a way: instruct the patient to place their head in your lap, then gently raise the eyelids with your fingers according to your skill, and let the eyelids be gently doubled in this way:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two threads in one piece according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully draw those veins out with force, and wipe away the blood little by little, until you see the veins move outside of the eye; and be careful not to wound the eye with the points of the tweezers, and perform this task at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut more than the veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye a mixture of green and red bile to corrupt what remains of the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to gather all of it in that hour, then make a plaster for the eye with calming ingredients for eye pain, and leave it on for several days until the pain is eased and there is no fear of inflammation; then begin again according to this method that was described earlier until it is healed; and this is the form of the procedure.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The experts call a fistula of the eye "arissati"; when you cure it by cautery and hot medicine as I mentioned before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to it: you should lance the abscess where the pus needs to drain, and remove all the moisture in it until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the instruments needed for this procedure, which is called "aspre chief", and make it in the shape of a blunt probe, pointed like a file as shown in the following form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Place the probe on the affected bone and turn it between your fingers, pressing down firmly until you feel that the corruption has been removed, do this several times, then apply drying medicaments.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the wound is closed and flesh has grown, and the flesh of the wound is closed, and it remains so for forty days, and it does not become inflamed or suppurated, and no bad event occurs, know that it is healed; if not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose in this way: by uncovering the bone a second time with iron and sharp medical instruments, and when it has been exposed, take a three-pronged fork as follows, and let the head of the fork be made of iron with three angles, and let the handle be tapered to a point as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 then place it on the bone next to the eyebrow, and move your hand away from the eye pupil, then turn the whole stylet until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the sensation of wind exiting if they hold their hand over the nose; and then restore the location with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens in the area, then the matter goes to the nose; making it a lighter matter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open wide all around and there is no disturbance or decrease in vision, then bind the patient, then cauterize, then apply suction cups or leeches without causing harm, then place a bandage made of vinegar, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla on the eye, and then apply pressure to the eye and cover it with cloths and bandages; and the type of cloth is such that you take soft cloths and fold each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the amount of cloth needed for the eye; then bind it tightly with a strong bandage, and reapply the suction cups without causing harm; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the bandage softens, tighten it significantly; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good; if not, reapply the bandages and cloths and bandage and suction cups until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of retinal detachment
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the growing membrane, it then appears, and comes out like a grain of resin among the papers, and is frightening to see; therefore if you view the rupture, the procedure is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then place another needle where there is a double thread from the eyelid; and have it pierced, leaving the first needle in its place according to the disposition; then cut the hole of the double thread and tie one part of the eyelid around it, and bind it tightly, then remove the needle and place a wet linen cloth soaked in egg on it; and leave it until the thread dries with the eyelid, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is bound by the eyelid with a circle of cloth on both sides until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye becomes very prominent, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from deep within the eye, and let the watery humor run out, and the eye will descend and enter in quickly; then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Here's my attempt at translating the revised sentence:
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bubble that forms in the eye appearing like descending water, but it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on an appropriate chair and straighten up, then hold the head with both hands and move it until you see the bubble coming above to your eyes; then let it be stuck, and let the light not descend and fall, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bubble is not arranged as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 if make sit the patient between your hands, then take the thin spatula and puncture through the horny tissue up to the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny tissue and the cornea, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and honey, then heal with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have similarities of the waters in the division, and that which is necessary to pierce; so act according to the health (condition).
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and cover the healthy eye very tightly; then place the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eye is left, or on your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the cornea by the size of a thread in that whiteness of the eye at the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of the almagda be to the depth of the measure from the pupil to the end of the darkness; and this is the cornea of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the horny tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 if the water recedes now, the patient will see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a short rest, and if the water rises again through the second passage, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and no longer rising, gently extract the almond while turning your hand little by little; then put a little bit of gemstone water in it, and raise the eye upwards.

Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, apply common bread soaked with egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, because there are some men who have too hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which this is the shape:

And then only pierce the ligament, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put in almagre (a type of medical powder), as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, in which they sleep on their back in a dark place; and be devoid of all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not at all necessary that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 if pustules occur, let the eye be unbound before the seventh day, and apply a compress of that which soothes a pustule; and when it has calmed, let the vision be unbound and place a bandage on its side to cover for some days, and always remain in that darkened room.

de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes various kinds of swellings and blisters are born, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such kind with flesh turned black in color, and also flesh that is soft with good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Then in the case of such a limb that is numb, and not inflamed, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands with their back towards the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply a leech to those limbs, and draw out the blood; then collect what you can hold in a delicate spoon-shaped instrument on one side, until you are certain that the limb is completely drained.

And if any part remains that cannot be cut, open it entirely with one of the thin instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood ceases to flow and all growths are removed, then throw salt and water or wine on the nose.

If the nose does not drain and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; but if moisture does not flow as it should, know that there is a growth in the bone above, which the instrument cannot cut: then you must insert into it a moderately thick linen thread, tied firmly with thin thread, with spaces of about a finger's width between each knot; and place the patient's nose in the snow up to its power, and pull on the end of the thread until it comes through the snow inside the mouth; and children often do this in school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the head that comes out of the snow with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other by feeling the nodes on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Perform this procedure so that you know the wound has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the sutures, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all remaining flesh; and then place a strip of willow on the nose for several days until it heals, and if drying medicines are needed, use them; and this is the method of the instrument to purge the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, such as a funnel, and the spout similar; and if you wish, make a closed funnel, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a sickness is born in the head of the nose which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, so that it becomes an obvious thing to see; and therefore you should lance it at the beginning and extract all of it, then place the cautery or hot medicine on the wound; and if you delay lancing it until it has grown large, beware if it is hard, with a dark color, and poor sensation: do not touch it at all with iron because it is an abscess that has become enlarged, because when you lance it even once, it brings great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is easily touched, not of dark color, and you see that you can completely lance it, then empty the patient's nose and carefully lance it without fear, and cure the wound with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose has been lanced and sutured
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it is of little use, except in some men.
