Then, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together in a stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then you must cauterize all the edges of their connection until they heal, then bring the two lips together in a stitch, and bind it, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and ground incense on it, and place a piece of strong plaster or any other adhesive plaster on the powders, and leave it on until it dries through it, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is such that you approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in abdominal suturing; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men, hard abscesses like grains of pepper appear within the lips, either small or large; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision at each node, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply a poultice of powdered vitriol after the incision until the blood is stopped; and then apply egg white, and cure the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often a swelling of the flesh of the gums arises, which the ancients call "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow out; then put vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders on the wound; and if this flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, you should cut it again and cauterize it: for it will not return after cauterization. Here are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of hardened or indurated swellings/tumors. "Sordens" is a medical term used in Old French and Latin to refer to hardened or indurated swellings or tumors. It can be used to describe various conditions such as abscesses, cysts, or other types of growths that have become hard or difficult to the touch.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, green, and blue-green, so much so that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; you should make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and clean the visible teeth and scabs until nothing remains; and similarly for the blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there at the first scraping, that is good; if not, then start again on the second and third day, until everything has been removed; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for cleaning, depending on what the task requires, because the shape of rasps used to clean outside the teeth is different from those used between the teeth; and have all these shapes and others prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when you cure the tooth of its pain, to delay pulling as long as you can, because one should not do this hurriedly; for it is a very important substance up to the point that there is no excuse for damaging it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then, when the patient is about to pull, you should make sure that you are ready with a pushing finger.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often, the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is a toothache and have the good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not go away, until the root of the bad tooth is drawn out, as we have already seen done by these surgeons; and when you are certain of the painful tooth, you must cauterize around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum from all sides; then, pull it with your fingers or fine tongs, first at the root and pull until it is loosened, then securely fasten the tongs; and have the patient's head between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After pull out the tooth without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you should fill it with rag strips, where the holes are; and gently tighten it with pincers, so as not to break it when tightening; and much bleeding should be worked around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and bring greater pain to the patient due to the wickedness of the root than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act as ignorant doctors do, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth cartilage and do not bring what we have mentioned; but instead bring about great illness due to the remaining roots or breaking of the tooth, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which frequently happens, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should be long and thick-handled, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth. And these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick-handled so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of strong iron, and serrated to hold (the tooth) firmly.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains to be pulled, you should place cotton soaked in butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the place is softened, then apply tongs called "algefri," which resemble a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, in this shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all the tongs, then you must expose all the flesh around the root and place in it the instrument called "althali", that is, a scalpel. Here is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and sturdy so that it does not break, and if the roots come out through this, it is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which the forms are described hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one uses this instrument that has two prongs, of which these are the forms:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools that are in front of the teeth's root, and of this instrument that looks like large pliers, of which these are the forms:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that there are many dental tools; and also other unmentioned tools; and the wise master will find his own instrument according to what his work and the disease require, for there are such diseases for which the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of causes. And one does not break the cart or any other bones where they rot, but instead seeks out the necessary instruments that I mentioned, and helps with gestures, of which these are the forms:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and able to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but instead can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, then use all of this instrument for it.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is not erupted after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; but if it is protruding along with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is shown here, similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And wrap the cloth around your finger and place it on the tooth for several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that it can be filed down, file it with a file like this one shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth gently with this file for several days so that it does not move until it falls out; then use a smooth plane at the end with any smoothing tool, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, you must file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth falls out.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth loosen, either from being struck or from falling out, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the patient's teeth on top of the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again from where you started, and pull gently but firmly with your hand, so that they do not move at all; and let your thread be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then bind the jaw with a thread using pliers, and align it, and place it between the healthy tooth and the loose one, and position it so as not to cut the tongue; and keep it tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, then tie it with another thread; let it remain and serve in this way all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of aligning two healthy teeth and two loose ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is put back in its place immediately, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled interfere, and sometimes the shape of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed in the empty socket and constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tongue ligature
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes there is a ligament below the tongue, which one is born with, or by accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the mouth of the patient, hold their head in your hand, and lift their tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment, and if there is hardness or a knot, and this is due to a healed wound, put the hook in and cut the ligament wide; and make sure that the incision is not too deep, for the artery is beneath it; and when you have done this, apply a compress of rose water and oil, or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue; and let the patient change it every night, so that the ligament does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if there is a bleeding disorder, place vitriol powder on the wound; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for that; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of fusse color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, throw in the oncine, and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to your work, put vitriol powder on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the limb easily and gently, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes abscesses called "godath" come inside the throat, and they are properly called the "two almonds". And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and of a pale color, do not touch them at all with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it at all with iron, to avoid bleeding; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will remove it, or it will break open by itself; and if it has a pale color and the root is fine, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check whether the hard abscess is calm and at peace.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit down in front of the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and have them open their mouth and take the surgical instrument in your hands, and press down on the tongue with it, covering the entire instrument; it should be made of thin silver or brass, similar to a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and you press the tongue down with all this instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the oncine and insert it in the almond, and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, which is in the form of forceps; and yet the heads are crooked, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and they are made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool at hand, take iron pliers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and once you have clamped one of the almonds, clip the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, and vinegar, and if there is bleeding, gargle the patient with water or the peels of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then treat it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, clip them then as you would clip the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was in her throat, specifically an abscess of small size; and she had tightly closed her entire throat so that the woman could not exhale through the blocked passage, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she had remained in that state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had protruded two grains through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened then and quickly inserted one probe into one of the nostrils, then pulled it out through the nose with a great quantity of pus; I then inserted another piece in the other nostril, opened her mouth and pressed down on her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut off a portion, and only a little blood came out; and thus, the passageway in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut away at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess increased again and filled up the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; I then tied it off and cauterized it inside her throat: it remained stable after that; and I left those parts, not knowing what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is beneath, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help at all, and you see that the main abscess has calmed down and it is thin, then you must cut it; and the one that is rounded and not elongated; and it is blood-red or the color of a boil or black, then you must avoid making an incision in it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, as I have said, you must make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it down, and cut it at one of the two points that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you do not cover entirely the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cover more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being covered (i.e. having a bandage), then you should use strategy in performing the cauterization while causing minimal fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of the cautery is with a sharp point.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And let the patient put their head in your lap, and then press their tongue to the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and moisten it with live coal so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and apply the tip of this instrument, which has the following shape: [a diagram/illustration follows]
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a hair or piece of cloth placed on the patient's head, such as the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument containing all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat and cause harm. Then keep your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye for half an hour, until you see it turn black and the bites of the medicine are calmed down; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with the cotton into the wound until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to reapply the cautery of the medicine, then do so, and after cauterizing, wipe around the eye with cotton embedded in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargling until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cauterization if it is treated with fumigation in this manner: take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and elder and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them in one pot, and add water, and bring to a boil. And let the pot be well glued with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the eyes be held in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is made dead; then begin to reopen it frequently, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it unless the abscess has cooled down.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an eggshell in the head of it, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to harm the mouth, and this is a good cure together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat; then you must extract what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what is not visible and has lodged itself in the throat, you must make the patient vomit after the food has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of leather, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will solidify and then you may extract it; and if it does not come out as we have said, then take an instrument made of wood in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and hold the head high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, nor force the bone in, and move the patient's mouth to see where the object is; then have the patient insert the instrument, so that he knows where the object is; then insert it downwards or extract the object with the entire instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's veins.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the veins are treated with medicine, as I mentioned in the division; and when this does not help at all, then look at the patient's throat in the sun, after pressing their tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see a vein, then draw it out with a small lancet, or with delicate tweezers that are suitable for this task.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that is not effective, then take a boiled chicken neck and place it in the patient's throat, then apply a hot iron to the end of the neck and repeat this frequently.[Notes:The translation "hot iron" for "I fer chaut" may be anachronistic. A more accurate translation might be "red-hot iron".]
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And have the patient drink water throughout the day.[Notes:The word "teigne" means "to dye", but in this context it likely means "to give to drink". This is an example of how words can change meaning over time, and how understanding the context of a sentence is crucial for accurate translation. ]
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the tongue senses the water, it will drop down.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not drop down as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will soon drop down.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the method of fumigation is as follows: take a pot with hot coals in it, and cover it with a perforated cloth, with the hole of the instrument placed in the opening; then apply the fumigation, and have the patient place the end of the cane in their mouth, closing it so that the smoke does not escape but reaches the tongue; and soon the tongue will drop down, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times. Allow the patient to experience thirst and eat salty and bitter foods, but do not give them water; then it will be necessary for the tongue to come out using this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the vein, it is when you can see it, similar to curved tongs so that they can enter well in the throat; and have a resemblance to a surgeon's beak, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many similarities of abscesses exist, according to what memory comes after from one and the other in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two manners, one of which is in its very likeness, and those that it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is for the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For the abscess of the head is different from that of the lower part, and the abscess of the fleshy place is different from that which comes in joints, and each one must be judged according to the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its development; and there are such ones that must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their development, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses come near joints, and are left until they rot around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupt, which causes constriction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 Or if the abscess is near the main member, and you delay the perforation until it is rotten, it will harm the main member; or if it is near the foundation, perforate it as soon as it is rotten; and one should not pierce an abscess that has grown without digestion being completed, except for one near the foundation, so that it does not rot inside and become long and form a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the lessening of the fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the incision at the lowest point of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be deep and through the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and on all sides where there is no cavity.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the puncture until it is firm after complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you puncture it before this, the body of the pus will be prolonged, and it will be full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is some abscess that is punctured according to the width of the body, according to the need of the limb.[It is unclear what exactly this sentence means without more context. It could mean something like: "And one should puncture an abscess according to the width of its body, depending on the needs of the affected limb."]
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small holes; and for large abscesses, large holes, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that require cutting out the core and covering it; when it has become as a cloth, and is mortified, then one must do similarly as for boils: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, so for abscesses of glands; and if there are such that require a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 For those who have no head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all of the pus in that hour, but instead draw out some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this multiple times, increasing the amount each time, until all of the pus has come out; and do the same even if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman, or small children, or old and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit (i.e. breath) sometimes jumps with the issue of the wound, which may cause the death of the patient, and you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have lanced your abscess, clean the wound and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a simple cut, then apply bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many holes, then you must put in each one a tent so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of skin, and you have sewn it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or linen cloth shavings without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold and fresh water, wet a cloth, and apply it to the wound frequently.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned in light doses from this book. If it is wintertime, and the area around the abscess is very sensitive, you should apply warm, wet tents and cloths soaked in wine and heated oil. If it is summer, and the area is fleshy, then apply wet cloths soaked in water and oil or wine and cold oil for up to three days, as we have said. Afterward, release the abscess and dry and treat it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here ends the chapter.
des soros	abscesses (from the Greek "abscessus", meaning a departure or separation)
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where small abscesses come out of the skull, and are shaped like meshes, such as the wattle of a chicken, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 Some of them are fatty and fleshy, where there is moisture like pustules; and some are hard and stony when cut into, and there is no doubt that the artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the procedure for cutting is that you should test every instrument called a "trocar" to see what it contains, as follows.[~Could not understand the symbol '~' in your response. I am assuming it does not affect the translation and ignoring it.~]
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, then they make an incision above the long one.[~Could not understand the symbol '~' in your response. I am assuming it does not affect the translation and ignoring it.~]
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is evacuated, scrape off the skin without leaving any of the tissue that contains the moisture, for it will return if anything is left; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and change the dressing that has remained from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you are certain that nothing remains from the night; then cure the wound with appropriate ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess contains pus, cut it in length as follows; and insert your fingers, and peel off all around, and devote all your effort to extracting the pus that is inside; and if an artery opposes you, do what I have told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same for the abscess if it is hard, and in cutting and caring for it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, for they produce little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if there are some abscesses in the head or neck that have no moisture, such as those I have described on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough and white stone, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck any of them, they would have caused as much damage as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses coming to the head, except those that come on children's heads and at the roots of ears, let the incision be always in the lowest place possible so that pus may exit; and treat them as appropriate.[strike]Et quant tu verras que li aposteme est enfleiz et enflambez de grant dolor, si conbien qu’il ne puist durer ne souffrir incision ou taille; et on apperceit bien que la bowe s’en va, et que il est plain et cuirasse de grant chaleur. [/strike]And when you see that the abscess is swollen and inflamed with great pain, so much so that it cannot endure or tolerate incision or cutting; and it is clear that pus is leaving and that it is full and hardened with great heat.
des scrophules	"Des scrophules" is not a sentence in Old French, but it appears to refer to scrofula, a disease characterized by tubercles or nodules in the lymphatic glands of the neck. The word "scrofules" comes from the Latin "scrofula," which means "broken neck." It was commonly believed in the Middle Ages to be curable by the touch of a monarch, and was also known as the "king's evil." A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have ophthalmia, it is necessary that the incision in the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided; and no help can be done through this, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are obstructed by abscesses, whether they are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the windpipe channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation, which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui. Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien. Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus. Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Then those who contain moisture should have their hair cut in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and apply a suitable ointment until it is healed.[FAQ]
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like those of scrofula, incise them as we have said in the section on scrofula incisions, and if the wound turns out to be gaping, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When an artery is damaged and the skin above it is stuck down, abscesses often occur, and the same happens when a vein becomes swollen and inflamed; this can be recognized when the abscess is long and deep, and feels hard to the touch; if it is due to a vein, it will appear red on the surface; and it is foolish to cut into this abscess, especially when it is located under the armpits or groin, in the neck, or many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it is necessary to avoid the iron cure and also the one at the head, and in the one inflamed by an artery pierce through the skin; then make an incision along the groin, and neatly separate the artery from the surrounding tissue until it is exposed; then place a needle underneath it, and make it penetrate to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then insert the probe in the space between the two ties until the blood within comes out, and let the abscess be released; then dress the wound so that it heals well, until the ligature falls off; then treat it with a suitable ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, then stain your hand with what you can collect from the abscess on all the skin, then insert the needle underneath the place you hold with your hand, and make it penetrate, and have a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I have told you, with one of the two ends of the two-stranded thread; and if you fear that the threads might come loose, then insert another needle underneath all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cut the abscess so that the excess comes out, then cut off the excess skin and leave what is tied; then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then treat it with compresses and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves[Note: I am not providing any comments or contextual information about the text, just translating the phrase as requested.].
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can develop in the artery and vein, an abscess can also develop in nerves when they are wounded or from excessive exertion and similar things.[Note: I am not providing any comments or contextual information about the text, just translating the text line-by-line into English as requested.].
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more frequently in shoulders and hips and all places where there are joints, namely, swellings, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and is in various dispositions without pain; and when one strongly constricts it, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but beneath the skin; and it can move in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and a joint dislocation should not be covered with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and one that is in the head or forehead makes the skin bulge.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut into its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a string and flay it, then remove it and stitch the wound closed, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large, hanging abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes there appear in the belly and not elsewhere small lumps, and it is a disease called "funge" due to its resemblance to them, and it has thin roots, and large heads; and some are small and others very large; and I saw a man who had two such lumps in his belly that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were jagged, and moisture was constantly flowing from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six ounces, and the procedure in cutting into it is to observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the flesh is white and moist and of fine roots; then cut with a large spatula, and have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in cutting, there often comes a flow of too much blood, and if the blood flows excessively, then hurry with the cauterizer; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of the iron, then take a well-made flax thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not cease to tighten the flax thread until it cuts the artery, and this will happen without causing pain; and if the roots are thick, then there is fear of cutting even through the belly, but you can well cut only half, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the thurl which is of foxy color and of poor sense and lax regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the abscess bursts open
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of a swelling comes from a cauterization of a wound or a split of an abscess, and it is located on the belly and in some parts of the bowels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it is due to the rupture of the abscess and the opening of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with hands, it recedes and then returns, and perhaps it becomes constricted, and greatly swells at the entrance to the bath and after heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and shows clearly when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the treatment consists of observing whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 So you must let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the boil, you must instruct the patient to fasten a cloth around their throat and lie completely flat. Then, tie a bandage around the swelling, and have them lie still between your hands. Next, walk around the area you marked for the incision, then place the middle of the abscess above the large hook; then bind it tightly with strong thread or silk cord, leaving one end loose. Perform the incision on the stretched-out part of the abscess, and insert your index finger to search for the intestine. If you find it caught in the thread, release it and push the intestine back into the stomach. If you find pus, use the hook to remove excess fluid; if an artery or vein hinders you, carefully move around it and then return to your work. Insert two needles with strong threads crosswise where you want to pierce, then pull on the abscess in four places using the needles as anchors. If you see pus, remove the needles and leave the opening until it rots away, allowing dead tissue to fall out; or cut it away when it becomes thin and rotten. Then treat the wound as necessary, cover the wound, and suture it closed.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancres and how they should be treated with medicine, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and we say that the chancre worsens in the groin, and great caution is needed in its treatment. And the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre found on the breasts, thighs, and similar places, it should all be removed when it is in the beginning stages. And when it has grown and become old, one must not approach it at all because I have never been able to heal any of them, nor has anyone healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you first purge the patient of black bile once or twice; then make them sweat if they show clear signs of indigestion. Then prepare the patient for the procedure by having them drink one good laxative. Next, throw your leeches onto the chancre and remove all of it without leaving anything behind. Allow the blood to flow freely and wipe the area clean with your hand or some other object. If the bleeding from the incision in an artery or vein becomes problematic, cauterize the area until the bleeding stops. Then treat the wound with further care until it heals.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have previously said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioning "eclites"; and one should not touch the iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and hypostatic, for it is a deadly thing; therefore, when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and solution of the belly and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and they have no other illness but dropsy only, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed in this way: lift the patient up straight in your hands, and have the minister press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the sharp-pointed spatula in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut in two parts.
