a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be pointed, yet not so penetrating that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot bleed; then check if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the navel three finger-widths straight down beneath; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the navel three finger-widths; and if it's due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to the weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand throughout the entire width between the skin and the abscess as in flaying to the length of a fingernail or slightly more; then pierce the abscess until the instrument reaches the visible place, and that is the watery place, then pull it out and insert this instrument of which this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And is similar to a thin silver hook, and is made of light bronze or iron, and has a small hole in its lower part; and on one side, there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the wound is cut in the shape of a feather quill, and this is the form of the incision that scribes carve the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 At the top is the collector, so that when the instrument comes into contact with water, it immediately descends onto the instrument; then you empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than is appropriate at that hour, the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit by the weapon, or they fall unconscious, or approach death; but you empty it according to the quantity of its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength signify, and their pulse; then draw the instrument and hold back the water, and it is now held back by the cork that stops the hole above the syphon, which I have spoken of, which you pierce in this manner; then replace the instrument the next day, if you see the patient tolerating it, and draw a small amount of water; do this for several days, but be careful not to empty it completely.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and leave too much water, cure it with sepulture or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and dye it with drink; and cure it with drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes a child is born who has no opening in the foreskin, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary for him to have it pierced as soon as possible with a very thin probe according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then insert or replace an ivory plug very gently, and keep it in place for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary to do so, because the urine that comes out does not allow the plug to stay closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 If the hole is small, then it can be treated with an ivory plug, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the hole in its proper place are injured, because some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis, which prevents them from urinating until they lift their penis up; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the opening, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way to perform this procedure is to have the patient lie down on their back, then extend the head of the penis and stretch it to the width of a pen's feather, positioning the opening in the middle as it should be; and take care to avoid causing any bleeding which can often happen; if it does occur, stop the bleeding with a styptic and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these ulcers appear on the penis, and it is an unpleasant sight; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a delicate lancet and cut and clean them all, then put a piece of cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with diaphoretic ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is harmful, of putrid color and matter, you should apply cauterization to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cut it out, and if the ulcer is on the penis, with part of it beneath the skin and part outside, you should remove the part that is beneath the skin first; and when it is healed, then treat the part that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because when you treat it all at once, the head of the penis is not assuredly healed and may become pierced, leading to blackening and corruption on the penis and in the anus; you must cut away all that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a poultice of honey and flour made from pomegranate rind and wine, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, moderate the moon cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery is helpful for two conditions combined: that is, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must insert a reed cane into the penis and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair at the tip of the penis (which happens to those who have not been circumcised) becomes wet due to wounds or abscesses, then you should scrape it with an instrument called "cheveit" until the ligament is loosened, and release the head of the penis from all sides; and if this is difficult to do, you should scrape it with a spatula on both sides of the tip of the penis and the skin; then gently separate them and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water between them, which does not become wet again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a loosening of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work willingly and particularly on children, it is necessary that we do the best and easiest work for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children because they did not practice it in their law, and we have none but what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen that most masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around a dale, and with force, and with a novaculum; the cautery avoided it because there are two layers, and perhaps one is cut and the other remains underneath.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it heals over with a cover, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleansing around the dale, the point of the member is not assured; and at the cleansing of the nail, perhaps the iron slips and ruins the work, and many times it happens that there is no need for cleansing, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing done with force along the entire line of the thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the force cuts evenly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, cut evenly in the shape of an "I" while continuously applying pressure; but let the thread be well tightened around the skin; and the first step in this procedure is to make the child, if they are aware, think that you are only tying the thread around the member and not hurting them, and then comfort them in every way possible; then place the member upright between your hands and apply pressure between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the member and blow and pull upwards until the foreskin is over; then clean it well of the gathered dirt, then bind the area with a double thread, then bind it again below the pouch with another ligature; and hold it with two fingers by the second ligature at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then quickly lift the foreskin and pull the head of the member; then let the pouch fill with blood, for this is beneficial; and place powder on it and on the powder a piece of cloth glued with a half of an egg cooked in rose water, infused with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for cleaning is as follows: the two heads should be sharp and even, and the heads should be as wide as a thumb equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the cleaning is when the core comes out at the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail, so that the place becomes an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and what is beneath the groin is swollen, leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and gently flay it; cut as you can move it, and be careful near the groin area, it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of hardened things with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if one cuts too deeply with a knife and it goes beyond, it will not harm; therefore cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	for urinary retention.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, congealed blood, pus, feces, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to the stone that is in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should bend on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and his belly should be extended from above down to his back, and the patient should strain his abdominal muscles as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained for the expulsion of the stone upwards, due to which the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instruments that are called "syringe", of which this is the form: and it should be made of thin and light silver, like the feather of a bird; and the cane should be one palm and a half in length, and should be fine at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of urine discharge is as follows: take a double thread, and tie one end of it to the head of a wool or cotton cloth, and insert the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess of woolen fabric and push it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe further up to the bladder, and let the patient feel it reach the empty place, and this is not done in this order except for the fact that the conduit through which it passes is twisted; then pull the thread all the way out along with the woolen fabric, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it outside, and make the urine flow; and repeat the process until the bladder is emptied, and let the patient be relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or it is filled with pus, and you wish to distill water and medicine into it, use an instrument called a "clepsydra," which has the following form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; and the shaved place where the medicine syringe should be such that it stops well the rod without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and push in when necessary; and when you see your medicines being poured into the bladder, put the tip of the syringe in the moisture, and pull the tail that is inside; you will pull the moisture into the syringe, and then forcefully push the tail back in; the moisture will enter in, and come to the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the subtle form of the enema with which one enema-izes the bladder: it is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or brass, and the head (noisemaker?) is higher up; and below is the bladder or the spleen where it falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you want to use to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a strong double thread, and heat one corner of the moisture over the fire; then put the head of the enema into the urethra, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it roundly around; then put a strong string through these holes, then gather the circle like a bundle, and put inside it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	"of the stone" (I assume this is referring to a kidney stone or similar)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have previously said in the division the kinds of stones, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone stuck to the bladder, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stuck in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and sand appears, and the patient urinates with difficulty, and urinates frequently, and then becomes rigid; and there are many of these jumps in the foundation; and the healing of children is light until they reach 4 years old, and it is very difficult for the elderly, and it is easy for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary to first cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and raise them up, moving him back and forth so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and comes out somewhat; then have him sit between your hands prepared for it, and let his hands be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining downwards; then search for and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall at the touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is an adolescent; and insert it into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull on the collar of the bladder; then press with your finger, and push it out where you wish to make the incision.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press on the bladder with his hand, and order him to lift the hips with his right hand, and remove the skin underneath the hips on the side where the incision is made; then insert the scalpel, which has the following shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make the incision between what is between the hips and the anus, not in the middle but to the side of the left opening; and let it be directly above the stone, and your hands should be always on the hip or the anus, and let the cut of the lancet be wide in front, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps by pressing with the finger that is in the anus, the stone will come out without effort; and know that some stones have angles and edges: they are difficult to extract; and there are some that are swollen, similar to a gland, and round, for which the extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then at that place where there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump out, you must pull with pincers that are like a file at the top, to extract the stone so that it doesn't shatter; or you insert beneath it a thin curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot deceive it in this way, then widen the opening a little, and if the flesh is thick, constrict it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first place the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it needs to be sawed, and a larger wound needs to be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine comes frequently because the wound cannot heal; but still try to drain it, or break it up with tongs, as much as you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place on it a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then raise the patient up on their neck, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with oil and water, then cure it with a fine ointment and a basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if pus comes in the wound and corrosion, and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained in such a way that it comes out with difficulty: then put your finger in the wound and draw out the blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder and eat away at it; then rinse the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and help him in all ways you know how, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every hour that you care for him, that you bind his two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and fixed inside, and the urine cannot come out; then you should treat it as I have said before, that you cut it many times, it is excused from cutting for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have tried it in this way before.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a fork of iron in this form and make it with three sharp points fixed on one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra below the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then insert the probe gently into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe with your hand in the stone repeatedly, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken at once, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this because of some hindrance, then place a thread under the stone and another on top, then insert the rod next to the stone between the two ligaments, then pull it out, and untie the ligature, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the female stone (i.e. kidney stone or gallstone)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone becomes ingrown in women, and if it does happen, the cure is difficult and is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled midwife who can examine her, even if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a skilled woman in this hand art; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of the man, therefore a deeper cut is required, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, then you must take a very skilled midwife, and they are hard to find, and if you do not find one, then use a subtle male midwife; and present a wise pouch to her in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command from the examination of the stone; and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her hand into the rectum and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she must press it down with her hand, and command her to insert her hand into the patient's vagina, and seek and press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she should move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where it is easily accessible, and feel for the stone in that place; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and make the incision initially small; then push the arrow into the incision, if you feel the stone enlarge the wound as much as the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and with points.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 if you know the symptoms to diagnose the dislocation.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the vein swells, apply crushed vitriol to it and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, once the stone is out, and have with you the instruments I mentioned for extracting the stone in men to assist you in your task; and if the vein swells, and it is from the cut artery, put powder on it and bind it with bandages and strips of cloth, and do not resume this process, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, for perhaps the patient will die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has calmed down and the wound dries, then return to your work, until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnal hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramic aquosa is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white humor, which is under the core of the kidneys and contains the egg; it is called "syfac," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the kidney that we have mentioned; and this only happens in case of a cyst.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramic aquosa is due to weakness in the kidneys, causing the matter to spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there comes a swelling on the kidneys, and this moisture has many colors: it is yellowish-tinged, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white like we have said, then it is a ripe abscess, about the size of an egg, and the kidneys do not appear, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very cloth, the abscess is solid with a part of the egg, and for this reason, it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the buttocks and the white membrane, it can be felt well. Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, examine it with the entire square probe, which its shape is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the probe, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with iron, the patient must be bled according to their strength and the fullness of their body; then lay them on their back, on something a bit high, and place many rags beneath them; then sit on their left, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the loins; then take the spatula and cut the skin between the buttocks, cutting it long down to near the anus, and make your incision straight, dividing the skin of the buttocks up to the white membrane, and carefully flay it according to your ability; then pierce the membrane full of water with a large hole, and extract all the water, and then put in your probe, and stretch the membrane upwards; and touch only the membrane, not the loins; cut the entire side of it carefully, so that if you do not cut it well, the water will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the membrane; then bring together the two leaves of the loins with one stitch, then cure it as other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the eye corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie up the blood vessels that are suspending, in doubt of bleeding; then cut the eye completely along with the suspensory ligament, and remove the eye and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if pus has accumulated in two parts together, know that these are two ramifications; cut the other part similarly to how you did the first, then wipe away the blood and put a wet cloth soaked in oil of roses into the wound; and put another wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and place it on the two corners, and put folded cloths on top, and bind it all up with a bandage in the shape of this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths, and stuff them with loose wool in this manner and sew them at the waistband of the breeches, and let one of the legs hang down to the lower back, and the other to the side; and the other two corners on the two angles, and have all the edges gathered together in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this ramification is cauerized with cautery instead of iron cutting, and that is when you take a scalpel-like cautery tool, and cut the skin of the scrotum, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus contained in the abscess is exposed; then take the cautery in this shape, and pierce the abscess along its edges, and scrape it with this sharp hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike in all ways that you can, until you extract everything; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and be careful to avoid excessive bleeding, and be cautious as in the operation of cutting; and if any contrary thing happens, such as an abscess or bleeding or other thing, then cure what is causing the problem, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo the procedure due to its horror, then perform an incision, as I have told you, which is when you are certain, based on the signs that we have mentioned, that the watery humor is present, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then incise the abscess in its lower part over its entire width, and place the incision along the length of the body; and let the opening be wide, so that all the liquid can flow out; then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining liquid, then cure the wound until it is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the liquid to come out of the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or instrument used to draw water from dropsical patients, such as the one described earlier; and widen the opening of the wound, and know that the liquid will return, and gather after 6 months or thereabouts, and when it has gathered as before, and in this way the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the haunches (buttocks)
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the sectioning of this branch, there is fear in multiple ways, so it seems better to me to let it be; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	So I say that many abscesses arise in the body, including on the hips; and this is due to various causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It should be known that it is due to excessive acidic and watery matter, which is spread in the region of the groin or from a blow; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the body; and no pain is found, and yet it is a serious abscess; and perhaps it is one of those fearsome and hard abscesses, with a dark red color, and sometimes it comes from a rupture of an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is due to a rupture of an artery, it can be recognized by the hot disposition of the abscess when pressed with one's fingers; and one must not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 He who is affected by inflammation of the vein can be recognized by its swelling upon touch of the fingers, and one can easily make an incision based on this likeness, and on other symptoms; and it is necessary to cut out the core of the testicles, then stretch the sac upwards, and pull out the inflamed part, and free the suspensory ligament from all sides of the sac.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the sac is already hardened with these symptoms, then it is necessary to remove the sac and its contents; and if it is adhered to the sheath or within the vessels, it is necessary to free all of the attachments and roundly cut away the surrounding area.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the base of the kidney is at that location, then you must cut it all out and extract the ureter, as we have said.[Note: The translation "base of the kidney" for "naissance de la char" is an educated guess, based on context. A more literal translation might be "the origin/beginning of flesh".]
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your tasks are completed, apply the wound with wet wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then dress it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the haunches (buttocks)
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enclosed by a swelling resembling a hernia, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient moves with difficulty when they walk; and the treatment for this illness is as fearsome as the previous one, but we will still tell you about its procedure, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the suspensory ligament of the scrotum downwards towards your hands, along with all the vessels that are close to the penis, and tie it up firmly; then cut the scrotum with a sharp scalpel, wide enough to expose the vessels, and then dissect from both sides, as we have said in the extraction of the temples' arteries; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and bind it to the first place where the vein has come, and then tie it again to the other end; then cut lengthwise in the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as you would any other, so that some vessels remain nourishing the testicles; for by this no harm will come, and if veins appear on all the vessels, then both testicles must be removed; so that the urethra does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry out and cannot heal.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rottenness of the syphilis
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The events of this branch are due to the section that comes from the abscess or the extension on the belly in the area of the haunches, because of which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the hips; and this rupture is either from the abscess or from the extension of it, and these two ways come from many causes: either from percussion, or from jumping, or from coughing, or from lifting heavy weights, and from similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the abscess are that it happens frequently, for a long time, and not suddenly; and the abscess is even to the depth because the abscess attracts the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	"The sign is, when it is of the cutting of the abscess, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess is of diverse appearance under the skin, close to it, and this is due to the evacuation of the intestines and flesh from the abscess."
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	"Sometimes the intestines come out with the abscess and become trapped inside, causing great pain to the patient, especially when pressed."
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	"And in these iron treatments there is reason to be afraid, and so one must be cautious."
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the manner of the operation is that you instruct the patient to move the intestines into his hand within the wound, if he can push it back; then support his neck with your hands, and lift his hips; then extend his chest upwards, and cut all the skin from the groin longways; then insert hooks of the size you need for opening the wound into the flanks, so that the entrails can exit; then dissect the membrane which is beneath the skin of the groin, so that the white membrane is fully exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger into that which follows the groin, in that which is between the white membrane which is beneath the skin of the egg, and between the second membrane, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second membrane; and then move your right hand inside the groin and stretch the white membrane upwards to your left hand, and lift the egg towards the flank; and instruct the assistant to stretch the egg upwards, and untie what is behind the ligature; and with your fingers feel if any of the entrails are wrapped in the white membrane, and if you find anything, push it back down into the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten strands, and insert it in the rear part of the membrane which is after the skin of the groin; after the wound, then cut the edges which appear from the threads, so that there are four threads; then arrange them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the membrane, which we said is beneath the skin of the groins, with a strong ligature of two parts; then wrap the ends of the threads and bind them firmly with two parts, so that no vessels which nourish it can enter in, lest abscess come there; and put again the ligature according to the first long ligament, and after these two ligaments leave the membrane which is beneath the chest cavity one finger's width; and after all the rest according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part which is beneath the skin of the groin, so much that the fat comes out and the bowel, as we have said before; then apply wet wool to the wound, and put it on the wounds, and apply again the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes, the white abscesses that we have mentioned are cauterized after incision due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For it happens many times, and leave the ligament until it breaks by itself; and if it delays in falling, then warm water should be used, and apply what we have said, until it breaks; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnal hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the surgery using iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like the branches that are entangled in a vine, in such a way that you bind the vessels after the incision lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess with what works, until the vessels break; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes there comes a rupture in the entrails, as we have said, and the opening is visible; and none of the intestines descend to the hips, and if any do descend, it is little, and it repairs itself every hour; and yet if it remains too long in this state, then the wound or fistula grows, until the intestines descend; and this happens due to the extension of the fistula which is in the entrails, as we have said, for it becomes extended, then softened and swollen, making the opening visible and wide; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies on his back between your hands, then cut the swollen part of the rupture as large as the width of three fingers; and then remove the fistula which is beneath the skin that surrounds it; then take a rag and place it on the visible surface of the fistula; and press it deep into the stomach, then sew together the two openings of the fistula to the head of the rag, and sew them both; then remove the head of the rag, and do not cut or stretch the fistula or any other thing, as I have made you understand in the cure of the ramice of the intestines; then cure it by the cure for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, clean and care for the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The intestine is constricted and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is more useful at this point and closer to healing.[Here's the translation for the next sentence:]
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	for softening the skin of the haunches (buttocks).[Here's the translation for the final sentence:]
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the buttocks is weakened in some men, because the fat that is inside is weakened, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, to make the patient lie on their back, and cut the weakened skin that is above the natural wrinkle; then bring the two lips together with a suture, and if you see, first sew the excess skin of the weakened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between the stitches, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and let the thread fall out.
dou chastrement	of cautery (treatment using heat)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Be aware that castration is considered shameful in our religion, and therefore I do not wish to speak of it in this book, except for two reasons: one is so that the physician may give a knowledgeable response when asked about it, and know how to perform the procedure; and the other is because we often have need of castrating certain animals to assist us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I then say that castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the one we do by attraction, make the beast sit in warm water until the joints are softened and pliable; then pull on the extremities with your hand until they are set back in place and you no longer feel any resistance.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Of the castration by cutting: you must first tie the animal and press the skin of the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspending ligament. Then make a cut over each testicle with one stroke, once they have been well skinned. Leave some of the sack and the fine tissue that is on the vessels; this method of castration is safer than the one done by attraction, because in the latter case there may be some residual tissue from the scrotum left, causing the animal to still desire lust. Then cure the wound until it heals.[`enter code here`]
des hermofrodites	"hermaphrodites" (people born with both male and female sexual characteristics)
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphrodite is of two kinds in men: one kind has an opening between the two buttocks similar to the shape of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes urine comes out.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other kind is in women, and they have a protuberance like a penis and two buttocks.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for both men and women is to cut away the attached parts and cure them like other wounds. In the second kind of hermaphrodites, those in which urine shoots through the skin of the buttocks, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	I'm not sure what you are asking for. The term "tentigene" does not appear in the provided Old French medical text. Could you please provide more context or clarify your request?
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Tentigen is a growth attached to the genital area, which is too ugly to look at. And some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 It is necessary that you stain the superfluidity of the tendon sheath on your hand or wrists, and lightly cut it; and do not go too deep, so that an effusion of blood does not occur, then cure another wound until it is healed; and at another flesh that arises at the mouth of the wound, and apply it, and perhaps it will come out, and it resembles the shape of a cow's udder, and for this reason, the ancients called it "cow disease".

de erratique	I'm not familiar with any medical term or concept called "erratique" in Old French or in modern medicine. Could you please provide more context or clarify your request? I'd be happy to help if I can.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 It is erratic when the nature of a woman is not perceived, or the perforation is small; and it is natural at birth, or accidental due to disease, or it is caused by joined flesh, or subtle or thick syphilis, and it is made deep in the wound, on the sides, or below, or wherever; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps menstruation; and the knowledge of this is through the observation of the midwife.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If pustules are about to appear, they will be at your fingers or toes.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is a subtle syphilis and it is close to the two loins, then hurry and proceed as follows: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, with her legs spread apart; then pull the two loins apart strongly, so that the subtle syphilis becomes round and appears above the pustules; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the affected area, and have the woman lie like this for a day, so that it does not stick together.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the syphilis is hard and thick, then you must cover it with a spatula that looks like a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the stoppings are of fleshy nature, then suspend it by a thread and cut it; and have hemostatic medicines at hand, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg yolk; then provide a wide reed pipe, so that the wound does not close; and let it be like this for a while, and provide a tent of dry linen; then let it be treated with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when flesh grows in the wound, it should be covered in this way, if it is not inflamed abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an inflamed abscess in the wound, one should not apply fire (cautery).
des emorroides	Des hemorroides (of hemorrhoids) is a French term that refers to swollen veins in the lower part of the anus and rectum. Hemorrhoids can be internal (occurring inside the anus) or external (forming under the skin around the anus). They are often associated with symptoms such as pain, itching, bleeding during bowel movements, and discomfort while sitting. The causes of hemorrhoids are not entirely clear, but they may be related to factors such as straining during bowel movements, chronic constipation or diarrhea, obesity, pregnancy, aging, and a sedentary lifestyle. Hemorrhoids can often be managed with lifestyle changes, over-the-counter remedies, or medical procedures, depending on the severity of the symptoms and the underlying cause.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not ordinarily visible, and when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into a grape-like form; and we have previously mentioned their similarities, signs, and here I will say those that receive treatment.
