Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and grape-like forms, when they are inside the rectum and not felt, then they are not cured by iron (cautery).
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those that are at the opening of the anus, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.[Repeated text removed for brevity.]
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you should place the woman in a cool house, then stretch out the hemorrhoid with pincers, and cut it at its roots, then apply powdered medicines that constrict blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then place her feet on the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and egg yolk, and make a plaster to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if he constricts (the area), it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If not, apply cups to the back and breasts without striking (them); then take wool, soak it in a juice of plantain or a juice of elderberry with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess is at rest, cure the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and similar to a rough surface, if so, cover it as I have said with a cloth; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses on the groin
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscesses come to the human body, such as chancre and abscesses around joints, herpes, ulcers, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Then it is necessary for me to mention in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marris, which is not one of the abscesses that swell up; and if you want to know the work of the iron, look and see if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not rush to pierce, but let it ripen until the pain is eased; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have two small stools for them to recline on, and support their back and bring their legs together at the outside of the thigh; and let their hips be spread apart, and place their arms beneath their knees, and bind them well with a good ligament; then turn them towards the right side, and prepare the instrument that is used to open the mouth of the maris, which will be described later; and it is necessary that when you want to insert this instrument, you must first pierce the roof with the point to know the depth of the maris, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then the depth of the maris must be covered with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm them; and it is necessary to place the funnel of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and it is cut open by hand, you should cover it with a piece of linen dipped in oil; and when the boil is emptied, you should put wet bandages soaked in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound; and push the bandage deep into the wound and place a clean, wet woolen cloth on top of the boil and wound; then treat it with appropriate ointment for two days until healed; and sometimes the wound and abscess are cleaned out by an enema of water and honey, followed by boiled linen roots and aristolochia longa; and then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is located in the groin, be careful not to cauterize with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the natural form of childbirth and its signs, which are: when you see the woman pressing downwards and desiring to smell an aroma, then know that the childbirth is according to nature, and the issue comes out beneath its head, and the afterbirth with it. And when you see these signs, you should gently press on her belly so that the child comes out quickly, for when it descends beneath its head, the afterbirth follows, and the groin is cleansed of its impurities through good purification. And one who comes out in any other way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 For it happens sometimes that he comes to his feet, and the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon his belly, or often, and is turned by chance onto his neck, and in other bad figures; so it is necessary for the balneum (bath) lady to be wise and skillful in these things, and that she be on guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out of the womb headfirst, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a stool or have women hold her; and anoint her vagina with oil or cooked fenugreek, and then insert into her hands the small spatula of the following form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 and split the ligature, and cut the nail to the point where the moisture that is inside comes out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then one must give the woman an enema of fenugreek with oil of St. John's wort; then make her drink a concoction and cause her to sneeze, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if both arms dislocate, you should gently and frequently relocate them; and if they cannot go back in, have the woman sit on a seat, and lift her feet up; then tilt the seat upwards on the ground, and make sure she doesn't fall when standing up; and if the arms still can't go back in, and the child is dead, cut off the child's hands with the knife that is placed here, and extract the child, and also relocate (the arms).
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the child's delivery on its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes out on its feet, you should lift it up; and then gently turn it around until it is even; then take hold of its feet and stretch them gently and frequently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 If he can jump up to his hips, order him to take a deep breath and then make him sneeze; if he jumps up, so be it, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he is not able as we have said, then turn it back and forth until it conforms to its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily corrected.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if he does not jump as we have said, then take a mixture of althea and oil of sesame, and boiled gum, and grind all of it in a mortar; and apply it to the woman's privates, both inside and outside, with this ointment. Then have her sit in warm water up to her ribcage. And when she is wet below, make her a collar of myrrh and place it under her, leaving it on for an hour. Then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and pinch her nose and mouth, and gently press on her belly, for the child will now jump.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's birth on his knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this manner, place the bolster under its hips and often support its neck, let its feet hang down, and have it lie on the bed; then fold its hands across its belly, and remove the cushions from beneath, so that it is lying flat; and if the child does not move on its own, take its feet and move them vigorously, then move its belly upwards, and place your hands there; and rock the child back and forth; and tell the woman to pull gently until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child's birth that comes out with a hand extended. \\
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to deceive (trick) in order to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie down on the bed, and strongly bend its legs; then apply the medicine that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, then study how to bring back the hand; and deliver the child according to the natural shape, and make her sneeze, and tell her to pull gently until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's coming out on its neck, and having its hands spread out, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary for the doctor to take his hand, then press and release it gently, and lightly blow on it; and when they are even, place a small piece of raw meat and oil, as we have said, then make them move it slightly; and once you have done this, make them sit on a seat, and tell them to hold their breath; and make them sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all the second stage.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it comes out in this manner all the way to the second membrane (after birth), cut the membrane at your fingernail, until the moisture is drained; and if the child hangs by its face and neck, cut from the mouth so that it is not retained, and the child will die; then place the child inside as needed, and tell the woman to take a few breaths: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth canal
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four at once; and this is not strange, it happens rarely. (My translation)
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are strange things, and do not live long, unless they be named; I know what they are, that they may multiply, and are separated by the umbilical cord which divides them, which is attached to the belly; and sometimes they come out naturally like lumps, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out forcefully, so treat it as we have said, and let the balancer be skillful, and quickly and lightly do what he does; and do it in such a way that it may be moved to safety.
de plusors enfans	in several children[TIA-1]
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb as I, II, III, IV, V, VI, VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise one, and it is necessary for the balancer to know all this, because by chance similar things happen; and do according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you cure a woman of a dead child or swollen belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to do manual labor; then you need to know if the woman is of sound constitution, and if she has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should be placed on her back, and her hips lowered, and her legs raised; and let the minister attend to her from two sides, or tie her to the bed so that she is not hindered in the delivery of the child; then anoint the mouth of the womb with moist oils with muscillaige of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the balancer's hands with these oils and muscillaiges; then gently insert them into the woman, then look for a place where the navel strings are suitable to be tied, and take care if the child is positioned so that it descends on its head; then tie the navel strings to its eyes or neck or mouth or hard palate or under the beard or in the groin or near the ribs or sides, and if the delivery is on feet, then tie it to the middle fingers; and it is necessary for him to hold the navel string with his right hand, and place the basin between his two hands with his left hand, and gently insert it into any of the places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the form of the navel string:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 then place another pin crosswise, or a third if needed, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch it evenly by moving it back and forth, so that the wounds can come out, and make the pins sharp to hold in the wounds, as in this illustration:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if some part remains, anoint the wound with oil from one of your fingers and push it into that part, and pull out the other part; and if none remains, place this pin higher up, and do so until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be brought back by holding it, you should wrap it with a cloth until it comes out completely; then bind it at the joint of the wrist or ankle, and you should do the same for the other hand and both feet.[`questions`](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSe876g3fwWZxz0-aQqvuUYj_JbJj52K9GkX4ewM8yVlhAOcCw/viewform)
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and tight in the opening, or if they have a swollen fontanelle, then you should insert the pointed spatula between your fingers and make an incision in the fontanelle to drain the fluid; or you can use the instrument called "almidach," which is described with the other instruments or chapter that comes after this one. Do the same if the infant has a large head naturally. Then pull out the bones using pliers, and if the head pops out and becomes constricted by the forceps, then make an incision until the fluid in the swollen fontanelle drains out. And if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can. If their belly or chest is swollen, then you should pierce them until the fluid drains out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the delivery will be easy and the bringing of the child to the mouth of the womb will be easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is constipated in the belly or the breast, then you should extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision in the belly or the breast, until the moisture that is inside runs out; and if the other members are removed and the excrement remains, then the bailiff should put his hand deep into the wound, and pull it out up to the mouth of the wound; then he should insert a finger or two, and pull it out; and if the opening of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, then you should not work on it, but instead introduce moist and fatty substances; and apply soothing and softening ointments, and place it in warm and softening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the infant is on its side and you can make it even, then moderate what we have said in the living child; and if there is no power to do so, then pull it apart piece by piece and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done that, moderate what we have said in abscesses that come in the mare's womb; and if bleeding comes, then use a restraining remedy in water, and moderate other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	"And I saw a woman in whose womb one fetus had died and then a second one was conceived on top of it, but the second one also died." This sentence from the medieval medical text describes a rare case where a woman became pregnant with a second fetus while carrying a deceased fetus inside her womb. Unfortunately, the second fetus also died in this situation.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	"After a long time, an abscess came to her belly and swelled so much that it burst open, and she began to suffer greatly." Here, the medieval medical text describes a patient who developed an abscess in her belly after a long period of time. The abscess grew so large that it eventually burst open, causing the patient significant pain and suffering.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	"I was called to treat her, and I thought for a long time but could not heal the wound." This sentence from the medieval medical text describes the author's attempt to treat a patient with a burst abscess in her belly. Despite thinking for a long time about how to heal the wound, the author was unable to find a successful treatment.[/I>
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	"I applied a strong plaster and out came a bone, and after several days, another one did." This sentence from the medieval medical text describes the author's treatment for a patient with a burst abscess in her belly. The author applied a strong plaster to the wound, which caused bones to come out of it. After several days, more bones came out of the wound as well.[I>[The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it might be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I treated the wound, and extracted many bones until the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived for a long time like this, and occasionally she would pass a little feces from the side; and I only recorded this chapter because when the master finds a foreign object, he should know how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to put the fracture back in its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the press, with which one squeezes books; and with two turnings at the two cheeks of the two levers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 Nevertheless, let the horns of the restrainer be finer, and made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth of the bow be two fingers wide, and the edges of the limbs one palm and a half in length; and in the middle of the two limbs there should be two joints of this same wood, which are fastened in both, being half a palm long or slightly more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the bow to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, more slender and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, similar to the shape of pliers; and let there be two joints at the two ends, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the bow with all the instrument, place the woman on a bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then insert the two joints adjusted together into the bow, and hold the head of the instrument beneath her thighs; then work your hand with the entire instrument, just as you have done with pliers, according to the size that you wish to open the bow's mouth, until the ball does what it is supposed to do.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all sharpened and come in many shapes; and when the surgeon has prepared them, the work is then quicker and higher for the men because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessity is not to be excused.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained in childbirth, you should instruct the woman to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with some help, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she faints because of this, it's fine.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, take a pot, make a hole or opening in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the uterus, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, cascale and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in water over a fire; then place a reed or opening of the pot into the uterus, and the other end in the mouth of the woman, and suck until the vapors reach inside the uterus; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the pus quickly comes out.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this cure, and does not leave, instruct the nurse to wet her left hand in oil of cedar or musk of althea, and then put it on the wound, and seek the opening; and when she has found it, so take and stretch it little by little, so that the sore does not tear during the extraction; but it should be moved gently to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and become less swollen.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the opening of the sore is too narrow, we have said the cure is to induce sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not leave despite all that we have said, make sure not to force during the pulling; but it is necessary for whoever is at the sore's mouth to tie it to the woman's thigh, then enema it with theriaca ointment; it will soften and bring it out, and it will leave; but nonetheless, when it softens, a bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Then it is appropriate to use suitable fumigations for this person: some of the ancients have tried fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for the retention of menstrual blood and after childbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it looks like a weasel, and carefully place the head in the natural position, and stretch out the legs over the fire; and let the fumigation be above the coals, and the blister until it is burnt, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born who do not have a perforated anus, but rather it is stopped with a subtle membrane: then the midwife must pierce that membrane with her finger, and not with a sharpened instrument, and make sure the bandage does not touch it; then place wet wool soaked in wine and oil on it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will relapse, put in a piece of wood [or] plug and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to the rooms (chambers).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these stoppages come from sudden wounds or abscesses; such a stoppage needs to be covered and treated, as we have said with the piece of wood [or] plug.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in the anus / rectum
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodular and grow near the anus outside or in the space of two parts, whether it is one fistula or several; and when this nodulation is old, it works, and still has white moisture or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that there is a discharge or flatulence when the patient makes defecation, and perhaps in jumping, a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and up to the groin.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus is recognized the fistula in the anus, and not in the anus: and that is, you insert your index finger into the anus, and insert a thin needle of copper or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is tortuosity, insert a thin probe of wood or horsehair until you feel it with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no pus, gas or liquid comes out of the opening as we have said: know that it has not pierced; so hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has penetrated to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, if the urine leaks out and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it has pierced to the joint of the thigh, then the probe comes to the place; if there is no tortuosity and pain around it, then it is already healed, and medicine or ointment will not help; and in these fistulas there is no cure except through labor and the folly of false doctors who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In the one who is not Persian and not ancient, there is hope of health through surgery, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies in your hands on their back; and lift the legs up to the thighs, and have the thighs inclined towards the belly; then insert a tent peg of iron, or of wood if there is curvature, until you know where the peg comes to.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the anus, then you should insert your index finger, and if you feel that the peg has pierced it; and uncover where you feel between your finger the abscess or flesh, then know that it is Persian; and do not work on it anymore as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 Always keep in mind that some can be cured, but it happens rarely; and the help that one can provide is to heat the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and insert it, very hot, into the fistula until it reaches the bottom; and do this twice or three times, until you are sure that the charred flesh, which looks like a bird's feather, is burned away; and then cure it with moist bandages smeared with butter, until the char comes out; then cure it with a spreading ointment for healing and joining flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed in any other way, and if the bandage enters but does not reach the finger that is at the bottom, and there is a thick covering of flesh or tissue between your finger and the bandage, and you see the fistula following the covering of the bandage; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the bandage forward, and then apply the cautery until it reaches the end of the bandage; and the bandage will be released and will fall out; then burn away the charred flesh that looks like a bird's feather, leaving nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood flows excessively and comes between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or medicinal liquid. (ET SI THE BLOOD OVERWHELMS YOU AND FLOWS BETWEEN YOU AND THE WORK, CAUTERIZE IT WITH FIRE OR MEDICINE.)
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 For the fire cautery brings about two good things: namely, the burning of joined cartilages, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then the healing of damp tents smeared with butter or crushed vegetables, until the place is healed and the burnt cartilages come out in the pus; then the wound is cured of hard, solid pus, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the depth of the fundament, and is removed from the body, place your finger in the opening and feel it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the abscess, and between two layers there is fabric or syrup or burnt flesh, or it is about to burst, there should be no hesitation but rather confidence and hope in one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the base, or if possible, you apply dressings and cure it as before; and do not dig too deep, so as not to cut the ligament holding the foundation, and cause unwanted discharge; then cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering which is cut next to the foundation, either with a dressing or with a pointed instrument; then clean the faulty flesh in the wound, as much as possible; then try to heal the wound and keep the fistula on the outside of the foundation: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas are formed in this way: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is next to the base near the skin above, take a probe pierced at the tip in this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted wire through the holes, and push the tent peg into the fistula all the way to the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is pierced in the margin of the base inside, then pull out the thread from this hole, as you insert your finger into the base; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two sides together, and hold them close to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and tighten it several times, until the threads cut through the flesh between them and fall off; then cure the wound until it heals and becomes clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce (on its own), make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not appropriate to cover the wound by making an incision so deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spiked spatula with which one forms the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Emorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the fundament, like a grain of resin, and there can be small and large ones, sometimes causing bleeding, and they can be outside or at the base of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and still there may be some yellow water or some blood, and they have the color of flesh; and the treatment for those who have them inside the fundament is to instruct the patient to strain when going to the chamber, so that the fundament protrudes, and the veins become visible; then hurry, and cut with pincers or hold it with your nail, then cut its roots; and if the hooks cannot hold due to their moisture, take them with a piece of cloth or cotton, or from a piece of camelot; and pull them out with your hands, then cut and powder them with some hot powders that are in place of cauterization; or you can cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, and cure them with other cures until it heals; and if the fundament cannot come out, enema the patient with a bitter and harsh enema to wash what is in the fundament, so that it may come out openly; when the patient feels ready, and when the veins are outside the fundament, then the treatment is easy; and it is to take them with your nail or pincers, and cut and cure as we have said, until it heals, and make the patient fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You should prepare the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it on a needle, then pull the thread over and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread beneath the needle, and let it be of sufficient size; and pull the thread tight, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to draw out any excess blood; then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote on the wound, and place it on the wound, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them lie down until they urinate, and when they have passed urine, cure it with ointment and other cures, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	(of) dried-up pus or feces/stool
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is dried-up pus in the intestines, due to constipation of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is not helpful.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you place the bark of a spatula or your nail on it, preventing it from becoming moist; then cure it until it dries as it should; and if it cannot dry, repeat the shaving more forcefully than before, so that it heals well and is scraped; then cure it until it heals.
dou fremit	of trembling.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A formica (ant) is a small ulcerous lesion that appears near the body and goes very deep; and sometimes it is found in the folds, and it feels like a dead frog, and spreads throughout the body, and more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the treatment is: take a quill from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather and place it on the frog (lesion) until the circle encompasses the entire lesion; then turn your hand around the whole quill while you scrape all around the lesion, and dig deep, pulling out the frog by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do the same with a reed of iron or steel, according to this form, and make it thin underneath and drawn out on top;
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not too piercing, in order to hold it to the finger, and press it; And if you wish, cauterize the stiffness, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema syringe
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	An enema syringe is never made of silver or brass, nor melted iron or lead; and sometimes they are small or large, according to the one who uses them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who use them in the care of children, and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small or large enema syringe is as follows: the wide end goes against the belly, in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And there is a dislocation where the belly is bound, as you see, and the feces are pierced inside; and has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and let the belly be where one puts the medicines of an animal bladder or parchment, and let it be pierced all around with small holes, and have between each hole a finger's width, then insert into these holes a strong thread of twisted silk in X or around, and bind the belly as if it were a sack; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then perform an enema; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister should press it with both hands together until it is all visible, then remove the enema, and lift the patient's legs apart, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it as much as possible; and if he sleeps through the night, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the stomach and the medicine quickly comes out, then administer it again until it heals.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are piles or a boil on the fundament, let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is the shape of the fine enema, with the skin stretched tight:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have previously discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and medicines, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.[INT] Et je dirai par ordre: les plaies des testes sont diverses de celles qui sunt a els autres luoiz du cors; et pour ce que li chief est plus nobles et plus delicat que nului autre luoiz, si covient il avoir plus grant cure et plus grant attentions.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are: a blow by a stone, cutting by a sword or knife, or a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from striking by a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then have it purged immediately of the cephalic itself if it bleeds slightly from the wound, and let the incision be on the opposite side of the injured part; and make the patient evacuate thick food and wine.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to be purged, let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine, nor eat meat or animal flesh; and place on the wound, if a hot abscess comes there, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, but it is fresh and has all its blood and is not moved by the air, then put a powder, which I will mention shortly; and if the wound has been moved by pus, then place some ointments on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword cut and similar ones, and its lips cannot be brought together with bandages, then sew them together with stitches, just as I will describe for wounds in the belly, using sutures.[Notes:
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone, and festers, and only holds together by a small amount, then cut it; next, cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rotten flesh on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut away all the rotten flesh and discard it, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, that cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loose, then bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: apply this powder that heals after the wound has softened.[StLiteralTrans\_7]: I would translate "li ars" as "the wound", but it could also be translated as "the surgeon". However, based on the context of the text, I believe "the wound" is the correct translation in this case.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is as follows: take one part of incense, two parts of dragon's blood, three parts of living alum, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly until it dries thoroughly and joins with all its blood; and then bandage it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes this is done only with lime, when incense or dragon's blood are not available, but the wound has already been treated by the doctor. (my translation)
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound has festered due to the application of fire, do not apply this powder at all; instead, apply some digestive ointments or a paste made from barley flour with water and honey until it discharges pus; then treat it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the fracture of bones comes with the wound, and it is small, then I extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound[ITR] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries. Try to guess what the text means and translate it line by line into English like this:
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If pain comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference with that of the head, unless the sinew of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy but to leave the wound alone and not apply anything restricting, for that harms the nerves and makes them retract; and nothing cold should be placed on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be mild, such as lime washed in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and also washed lime in soft water, and other similar stones, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and high up, full of pus, pierce it in a lower place; and if an artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, tie it off, and bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the passage remains, so that food can pass through, then sew up the windpipe on the groove of the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it to its natural shape; and then bind it appropriately, and leave it for some days, then cure it with discarded dressings until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, seek it; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound rots, and becomes loosened and straightened; and if the wound is fresh, powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, cure it in this way as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a lance or knife blow, and the wound is deep, look if pus comes out of the wound while the patient urinates: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it's not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it immediately, nor bind it tight to prevent the blood from clotting and returning to the heart, causing the patient to die quickly; but apply a drawing ointment, and change it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more; then no spasms, bad tremors of the heart or straining while urinating will occur; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Heal the abscess and other wounds, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; then heal it as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the belly, side or back, heal the part in front; if it is large, with sutures; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone, and has broken pieces, then clean the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are separated; and if they are not separated, then let the wound suppurate, which will make the extractions easier. And for wounds in other limbs, the judgement is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The ruptures of the belly are large, medium, and small; sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out from a large wound, and the suturing is more difficult, and often a small wound is worse than a large one, because the intestines are harder to put back in, if they are not put back in place piece by piece; because the intestines swell immediately upon feeling the cold, and are harder to push back in, and for this reason, it is better to leave the middle-sized wound open, so that the intestines can be more easily returned to their place. And know that the ruptures of the belly are according to four manners: the two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suturing of other wounds of the body and two other common sutures are specific to other wounds; yet they are more particular to the suture of the belly, and I will describe each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines protrudes, and it is difficult to put back, this can be done in two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in the following way: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only, or cook it in a decoction of wormwood, cypress, and pepper, and sprinkle the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes use this wine to tighten, and it is often effective in reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling spread, apply a poultice of warm water and crushed herbs, such as althea or mallow, for this eases the passage for little things; and if it is too tight, make an incision in the wound using the instrument used to cut piles; and the first treatment is to remove any excess tissue, cutting only when absolutely necessary; and this is the instrument's shape: [ (shape of the instrument) ]
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines protrude, return them to their natural shape and place, if you are able, for it is better to set things right.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large, and it is in the lower abdominal area, then you should make the patient lie on their back and place their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the lower abdomen, then you should place the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and likewise, if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, then make sure that the injured part is higher than the other. And it is necessary to manage in this way for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;
