et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, prepare what is necessary, then take a gentle minister who can hold the entire wound with their hand and bring the edges together. This is the common method of suturing, which is to take one or more needles, depending on the width of the wound, then leave a gap at the beginning of the wound and insert a needle where there is strong thread; and pierce the two sides of the skin with the two sides of the incision, which is inside the skin, so that you make it pass through that part, and bring the two ends of the incision together; then tighten a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring the two edges of the wound together evenly, and then leave a gap and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this with as many needles as you need until the entire wound is closed. The needles should be of medium size, between fine and thick, for thin needles cut through all the flesh, and excessively thick ones cannot penetrate well. Therefore, they should be of medium size. It is also important not to insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin, as they can open and widen the wound before it heals. Then clip the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and place bandages or cloths under the needle points to keep them in place until the wound heals. This method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds. For the second suture, it is common to use a single needle or two, and to bring the two sides of the skin and incision together on one needle with strong medium thread. And when you have pierced all four parts together, turn the needle back to where you started, in the same way that one sews fabric. Leave space between each suture equivalent to the width of a thumb. This method is known by people, and I sewed a wound that a man had on his belly, which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm's length, and two palms' length of intestines were protruding, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I set the intestines back in place after they had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed within fifteen days, and I treated it, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I placed clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you of the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle and insert it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced straight through, place the tip of the siphac or thread where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the inside to the outside; and the technique of this stitch is that you sew in the same way that a furrier sews furs, leaving the siphac on one side and taking it up on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of suturing, which Galen properly calls for, is as follows: some bring the two parts together naturally and apply one chief part of the suture to the other in such a way. First, insert a needle or chief part of the thread close by, and only pierce that spot, leaving the two sides of the wound; then turn the needle and make it pass from the outer part to the inner part, through the two sides of the wound; then make both pierce from the outer part to the inner part, through two other holes of the thread on the other side; and this is the stronger manner of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when the wound is in the middle of the belly, the sewing is more difficult than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is as follows, just like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh, with all its blood, so that the flesh has been moved by the injury, then replace the intestines and the cut; then put powdered charcoal on it, and if the flesh has been burned by the fire, then put on any available ointment until the wound closes; and wet the thread, and let the sutures and the mirach be tied; then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you don't have medicines, then put on old cotton, as soon as it begins to close the wound, and move it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then you should moisten a light linen with oil of temperate heat, or with rose oil, and place it around the edges, and beneath the buttocks; and if there is pain or corruption in the bowels, and this happens often, then purge him with warm wine and similarly if the corruption comes as far as the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the abundance of veins that are there, and the delicacy of the whole body, and its proximity to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the worm exits the wound, put it back in place as you would the intestines, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and turned black or blue, you should tie off the blackened area to prevent bleeding, since there are veins and arteries there; then cut away the part that is between the tie and let the two ends hang down from the bottom of the wound to ease extraction when the worm exits, and allow the wound to heal.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the boil;[Amazon Alexa Smart Home
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is swollen and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I saw that a man was wounded in the abdomen by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and became inflamed and developed into a fistula, from which excretions and gas were emitted; I treated it as best I could, and did not cease my efforts until it had healed and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it soldered, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but rather improved in a better condition, eating and drinking; and some experienced ones said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a manner: take strips with large heads, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the strip has opened its mouth, place it on the two edges so that it pulls its mouth shut; and then cut off its head, and this holds so that it cannot become undone, then put another strip in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 This joint, if it becomes heated in the interior, brings no harm to the patient, and one can bind the interior with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a way: take the head of this intestinal filament, which should be very dehydrated, and then tie the head of this intestinal filament to a thin thread of linen, then insert the filament into the needle and sew the intestine, and pull it taut in the incision; and this method of suturing is not outside the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no device or cure, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it matures, is commonly called a "fistula," and likewise when it breaks open and becomes hollow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is, according to its true nature, a hard and white nodule that is not painful, and is as hollow as the feather of a bird; sometimes clear and sometimes thick; sometimes shallow, and other times deep; and I have spoken in the classification of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is not without one of the Nine causes: namely, due to the small amount of blood or flesh; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the edges, preventing the growth of flesh; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or due to corruption being a form of pestilence; or due to the property of the region being slow in digestion, healing slowly, and swelling by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the cures with medicines in the classification.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to let you know the cure for a fistula, which is done by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that a fistula can happen in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the syphilis, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to some joint of the hands or feet; and there are some that come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all fistulas of this kind are of difficult healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach to the place I mentioned, and you have trust in the cure, and you recognize it, take an iron or steel probe, if the fistula is straight, seek it; and if the fistula is crooked, seek it with a fine reed probe, for reeds bend around curves; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot seek it with probes, irrigate it through one of the holes, for moisture quickly moves from one hole to another, and cleanse it; then seek it as well as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and if it is embedded deep, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from jointure, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of the places I mentioned to you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the abscess and the corrupt flesh that is inside; and then cure it until it heals, and if the fistula is deeply embedded straight in, then cut as deep as you can, then place wet bandages medicated with medicine that corrodes excess matter remaining at the bottom; and then apply irritants that draw healthy flesh, until it heals; and if it does not heal by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupt from the fistula, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If vein or nerve does not trouble you, nor the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, let the king (a surgical tool) touch it until all corruption is removed, then cure the wounded flesh with non-corrupting things until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns bent as before, know that you have not yet reached the bottom: uncover and seek until you are at the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; and there is no other device but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupt, and you can pull it with pincers, then pull it out with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, do not leave any; and if moisture makes it difficult, and there is no mistake or fear, cut into the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place a putrefactive substance on the wound and let it be until the area around the bones becomes putrid, and then the bones will come apart more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, then reduce the corruption until all of the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the corrupted area, and it comes up to the marrow of the bone, then it must be covered and protected until the corruption is healed, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 A young man of around thirty years old had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, such that matter came into the leg and caused a large abscess, and there was no opening for it to drain; but the physicians, out of their foolishness, operated on the abscess so much that it opened and a lot of matter drained from it, and it became a fistula, and a great deal of pus came out which all smelled foul and moist from the body; and many physicians applied treatment to it for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine among them, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines they were using to treat him, and the matter that was coming out through the fistulas in large quantities; and the young man's skin became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came toward the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I then hurried and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot came as far as the inside of the bone; I thought what appeared to me of the rotten bone was all of it, and believed there was no other corruption except what I removed; and I began to treat the wound with soaking medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; and I tried again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I thought it was all of it, and then I removed it, and I took care to heal the wound; but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and pulled it all out, then I treated it with medicines; and it healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to resume the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For through the evacuation (of blood) he often sweated, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone grew a hard flesh, and it was of good condition and caused no harm or contrary effect at all, neither in moving nor staying still.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way: take a bandage and strain it at the end of the bone that is visible, and command someone to pull it up; and place another larger linen bandage over the skin that is above the bone, and stretch it out so as to draw the rotten flesh beneath it, and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to operate, so that the knife does not cut the good flesh; and place a hot iron or board underneath the bone to cover the rotten flesh; and one should operate until one can see and feel the corruption, and operate again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupt and not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, reveal all the flesh; then put a piece of wood beneath, and then cover the corruption with thread from one side to the other, and let the thread be one finger's breadth away from the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupt joint, and cover the bone or what it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other option but to cut; and if the corruption is in the thumb of the hand, or in the thumb of the foot, this is a very difficult thing, but nonetheless you must examine the corruption, how it appears to you; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve prevent you; and know that there are many incisors and threads for cutting these bones, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size; and therefore, one must prepare an instrument for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the types of diseases; so consider the instrument that you need accordingly.
dou feu	of fire.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulders can rot away either from within or from without; and when you have treated this corruption with medical cures, and it does not improve, then you must cover the member down to the place where the corruption is, so that the patient escapes from death, or from the greater harm of the member's defect; and one sign of this is that the member becomes black, as if it has been burned by fire, and will then turn black in other members, spreading throughout the body; therefore, you must act quickly to cover it, and if it is caused by the bite of any venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and the like, and the corruption is on the digit, then you should cover it and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut with a knife; and if it goes beyond the knife, it is deadly, and no remedy is of value except for the amount of its strength; and do thus whenever the corruption comes to a foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut all of the foot; and if it rises in the leg, cut at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means but to let the patient die; and the way of cutting or binding the member is that you bind it above and below, and stretch one attendant's hand downwards, and another attendant's hand upwards, and separate the flesh between the two bands by a span wide, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or bind, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the binding does not touch the healthy place, and come to the patient without causing further harm or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs while you are working, then cauterize the area hastily, or apply tightening powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage and treat it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man once: he had a discoloration that looked like a burn from fire, and this corruption first appeared on his foot's toe, so much so that it spread to the whole foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he immediately bandaged his foot, and it healed; but later, the corruption returned to the toe of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied healing substances after cleansing the body, but the corruption could not be stopped; and he wanted me to amputate his hand, but I did not, as I had hope of reversing the condition; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he might die, for the man's vitality was weak; and he lost all hope and returned to his land, and bandaged his hand himself, and it healed; and I have only told you this story so that one may act accordingly if such a need arises.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes a abscess comes in the flesh, and remains so long that it makes a large collection of pus; and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus drains out, leaving the wound open, like a container; and the skin that is on top is as thin as delicate fabric, and does not reach down to the bone, nor to the nerve. Such a disease is called "sain", and is not called "fistula". But if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone in depth, it is then called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cut all around it, and similarly when it is thin, like delicate fabric; and it does not heal easily due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you think that the skin has become hard, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with an enema as follows: see if the breasts are large, and the swelling that is in it has a foul smell, then enema the patient with Egyptian medicine made thus: take aloes, oil, and turpentine, equally, and heat them in a vessel over fire, until the mixture becomes red and as thick as honey; and then take as much of this as you need, and mix it with water and honey, and give an enema to the breast, and constrict the opening; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then extract it by straining; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed; and sometimes enema with water of ashes, when this medicine is not available, and take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over it, then filter it, and give an enema, until you are sure that the breast is cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate this, either the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then give them an enema of water and honey with a little turpentine; or give them an enema of honey and wine mixed, so that the honey has the property to cleanse and purify, and the wine makes the flesh shrink; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleansed, then give them an enema of a mixture that causes the growth of flesh in it, and take emplastrum diaphinit, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or give them an enema of some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned in the treatment of ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tip of the enema nozzle cannot enter, then widen it a little with an iron tool, and insert a plug of Egyptian or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then stitch it and leave it in a place where the enema nozzle can enter, and if the opening that emits pus is above, then aim lower where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 For when the bowel is deep within, it does not allow flesh to protrude; and if you are unable to cover the wound beneath as you would like, then arrange it in such a way that the bowel runs to the lowest point that there is, for when the bowel is deep within, it does not allow flesh to protrude and if you are unable to cover the wound beneath as you would like, then arrange it in such a way: that the bowel easily moves downwards, and lets nothing of the bowel remain; and take consolidative medicines to place on the wound, and stretch linen cloth over it that covers the entire wound; then bind the wound tightly at the site where the incision in the breast is wider than the first time, then spread a gentle ointment on another cloth according to the size of the incision, and place it on the incision on the wound to lighten the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth that covers it until after many days; and the one who is above the incision in the breast, often removes it to release the bowel, and know what comes from the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in such a way and you see nature arise at the incision on the wound, then know that the breast has already healed and approach the bandages; and then unbind it in the morning, or the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast (female breast) hangs unnaturally after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle venoms linger for a long time, do not lose hope for their cure, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For there are some men in whom the healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and even the contrary happens; and if pus persists in the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healthy; and if the breast is slow to dry up, and is distant, then apply drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphoretic ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine. Take diaphoretic ointment and mix it with rose oil, and dilute it with equal parts of old wine; then heat it and use it; and this same can be done better with thickened honey when diaphoretic ointment is not present, or you take myrrh, aloe, and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire; and then spread it on a cloth and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer longwort and celestial lily roots, which are also called vetch flour and centaury; and use simple or compound medicines: grind them and make them into powder, and put them on the honey that I mentioned, and use them; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has penetrated deep, making an impression on the bone, or in hard members, or ligaments; then proceed to cure the fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 A panaritium is a abscess that arises beneath the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps in other fingers; and when it has grown mature, and one does not pay attention, then a foul abscess comes, and it runs and spreads until it reaches the base of the nail, and possibly even beyond; and the corruption reaches the bone, so that there is painful, stinking pain, and the fingernail becomes wide, and its color becomes black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you cure it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, then you must cut away with a knife all the remaining excess beneath the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail approaches the flesh, and begins to prick, and injure it, then you must place a rod under the nail to keep it from pressing into the flesh, and lift it up, and carefully and lightly cut away that piece of flesh, and apply heated and corrosive medicine to the remainder to remove all of it; then cure it with wound treatments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out and remove it, for as long as the decayed bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see that the finger is becoming gangrenous, then cut it in two at the joint as previously mentioned, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is crushed and swollen, and causes great pain, then you must first treat the injury; then cut the nail of the spatula shape by cutting across from above, but be careful not to cut all the way to the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if necessary, apply something to alleviate the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the swelling of the hand.[Comment: Here, "sourdoit" is an old French word for a swollen and painful area on the body.]
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two types of dislocations that can occur in the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy, and by chance there are some where bones are present, and sometimes there is a nail, and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or the growth occurs in some of the fingers' knuckles.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one that is born in any knuckle of the finger does not move, and the one that is born at the joint of the finger, by chance moves; the size of the fleshy one is small, in such a way: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	A person who is born with a deformity at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: you must take care of it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one that is born in the back of the last knuckle, you should first cut the flesh roundly until you reach the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the joints come from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from burning with fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 It is necessary that you shape that suture, so that the parts may heal according to their natural forms; then place between two tents or damp cloths wet in rose oil, so that they do not join together; or you place between two thin pieces of wood, until the wound is healed, as is appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of these two with the palm, then cut that swelling as you should.
des vils	 of low status, base, vile.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Veins are thick vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body; and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, it is necessary that you administer to them purging of bile at some point, and then treat them with basilicum (a type of medicine).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment with iron is of two kinds: one is to cut and let out the black blood; and the other kind is to raise the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The surgery is as follows: first soak the patient's leg in very hot water until the swelling subsides, then straighten the leg of the patient from above the thigh to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the vitality of the patient can bear; and then bind it up and instruct the patient to eat foods that cause black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and this is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The treatment is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then put them in a bath, and soak the leg in hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then make an incision along the long vein above the knee or below the ankle; then lift the skin with a lancet, and cut the vein from both sides until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then insert the stylet underneath until it is raised from the skin, and then gently pull it towards the incision, then cut again in another place above three fingers; then lift the skin above the vein until it appears, then raise it with a lace as you did before, and pull it towards another lancet as you did first; then make another cut, or several if necessary, then lift it, and pull it to the toe, then extract and lift it up to the second cut; then extract it from cut to cut, until it comes out completely, then bind it; and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, insert a needle with strong double thread, and bind and pull it, and insert it underneath a stylet, and turn your hand this way and that, until it comes out; and be careful not to cut, for if it cuts, it cannot be pulled out or lifted, and it will harm the patient; and when you have extracted it completely, put wet wool on the wound soaked in vinegar and rose oil; and cure it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the eye socket is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you should cleave it obliquely, but do not cut it completely; and pull it as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to cut into the eye socket is curved and does not cut through, so as not to injure the vein; it should be of moderate curvature, for if it were too thin, it would cut the vein. Instead, it should be as thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein runs down the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry soil where there is no moisture; and it may happen to arise elsewhere than in the legs, due to decay beneath the skin, as a snake or worm crawls between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes into the leg a very large inflammation, then the location changes and the vein begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the incision is made, you should wrap around it a piece of linen from 3.5 to 4 inches wide, and tie it, leaving the linen hanging from the leg. And every time it protrudes too much, wrap it again around the linen and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, but not at the root until it has fully come out, for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and rotting in that place, leading to serious illness. Therefore, it must be treated carefully, piece by piece, leaving nothing in the body. Sometimes this vein, when treated, is 5 or 10 inches long. Once a man came to me, for whom it was 10 inches long. When you cut it, insert one finger or a probe and pierce it down to the bottom, emptying the contents within, and apply anti-inflammatory medicine to that place for some days, then cure it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein, both hands rain (a term for profuse bleeding), and likewise when it appears in the joint of the leg or foot, and there comes a great flow, and then it stops raining (bleeding); cure it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "maladie de buef" (ox disease) in our land because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body, going up and down, and one can feel its movement from member to member, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and comes out; and it is engendered by putrefaction of certain humors, like worms and snakes and lampreys and ascarides in the belly; and there is doubt about its malice because when it moves through the body and rises to the head, and if it happens to come to the eye, it may enter and destroy the eye; and this occurs frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being cured and pulled, it cannot be done without pain; therefore, you should tie the place above and below with a strong ligament very tightly, then cut and pull it out, and if the wound runs deep into the flesh and you can't find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it can do is to run to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head by the eye, hold the eyelid down firmly below it, then cut and pull it out; and you should use purges for the patient made of resolvent medicines for bad humors, and beware of spoiled food that causes putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that appears in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and not long after, I saw it move up to the shoulder, more quickly than anything, just like quicksilver when it flows from place to place; the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then soon spread throughout her body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it would turn around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved thus member by member, for I had never seen this disease exhibited in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Nonetheless, I have often seen that people eagerly want to move from one pain to another, but I did not wish it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because women have dry bodies, and revealed veins, and therefore those constrained windings appear; and this is not apparent according to this reasoning to those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and well-covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if they reveal it to you as we have said, then bind it firmly above and below, and then press on it until that constrained windiness comes out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then have it treated by one who expels windiness, such as stinking pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and the parts of the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The varieties of them (arrows) are such that there are some with large points, and small, and hair-like, and barbed; and some that have two angles, and some that have tongues, and some that have pieces; and an arrow that falls in any member falls in two ways: either in a principal member, such as the head, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it (the arrow) falls in any place of these members and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear: then one must be careful in extracting this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when these bad signs do not appear at all, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater that is above the brain lifts up, it is when there is scotoma (a visual field defect), stiffness and dizziness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion in understanding, vomiting of bile; and perhaps it exits through the nostrils or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there is a flow of moist and white matter from the wound appearing like boiled meat; and if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of an arrow when it falls in the chest is that it is close to the left breast and feels as if it is stuck in a hard thing, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like a bird, and there is black bleeding, and cold sweats and cold shivering, and fainting: then know without doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that an arrow has damaged a nerve is: without foam coming out of the wound, the throat swells, the patient changes color and sighs deeply, seeking cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrows fall on the covering of the chest, it is near the ribs; and it causes great suffering and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrows fall on the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will spill out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrows fall on the belly, and if feces spill out of the intestines through the wound, there is no hope for a cure or in extracting the arrow.[In this text, it is mentioned that if an arrow falls on certain parts of the body, such as the stomach or the belly, and some undigested food or feces come out of the wound respectively, then there is no hope for a cure or in extracting the arrow. This suggests that these conditions were considered very serious or even fatal during medieval times.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrows fall in the bladder, and urine spills out of the wound, and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is deadly. In this text, it is mentioned that if an arrow falls on the bladder and urine spills out of the wound, accompanied by strong pain, then the wound is considered deadly. This suggests that during medieval times, injuries to certain organs such as the bladder were considered very serious or even fatal due to a lack of effective treatments.[In this text, it appears that the author has a practical and empirical understanding of human anatomy and the potential consequences of injuries to different organs. The fact that the urine spills out of the wound suggests that the bladder is injured, and the strong pain felt by the patient further confirms the seriousness of the injury. The author's conclusion that the wound is deadly indicates a bleak prognosis for patients with such injuries during medieval times
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms, neck, throat, shoulders, armpits, spine of the back, ribs, hips, and legs, are safe according to various conditions.[This text suggests that during medieval times, certain parts of the body were considered more vulnerable to injury or disease than others. For example, the arms, neck, throat, shoulders, armpits, spine of the back, ribs, hips, and legs are mentioned as being relatively safe, while other parts of the body may be more susceptible to injury or disease. The phrase "according to various conditions" implies that the safety of these limbs depends on certain factors or circumstances, such as the severity of an injury or the presence of a particular disease. This text highlights the importance of considering individual factors when assessing a patient's health and determining appropriate treatments during medieval times.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the tear duct at the root of the nose: I pulled it out and extracted it from the other side beneath the ear fat, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And I extracted an arrow that struck him in the fat of the eye beneath the eyelid, and the arrowhead was embedded, and I could not reach it except for its point toward him, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the patient was healed, and no harm came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears: I cut away the barbs and delicately managed to extract it, and the Christian was healed.[NOTE: The translation "barbions" is uncertain; it could also mean "feathers".]
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And I pulled an arrow out of a man, who had it lodged in his belly, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not worsen. I cut open near the arrow, extracted it, and nothing bad happened.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you see a man who has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound has healed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not affect his natural disposition or cause harm to any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And I saw another man, to whom an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound healed over; and he endured this without great pain; and many others similar to this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man of the prince's, which had fallen into his nose, and it was slightly slanted to the right side; and the arrow was fully embedded. I was called to the cure after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
