Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I searched it with a thin probe and felt nothing; and he felt a pricking and pain under his right ear.[ℹ️ Note: The pronoun "il" is used instead of "je" because the subject has changed to the patient.]
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a plaster of attratif and digestive on the wound to prevent inflammation, and the place where the arrow was became visible.[ℹ️ Note: The pronoun "li" is used instead of "la" because it refers to the wound which is feminine.]
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I applied the poultice for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I placed corrosive medicine on the wound for many days, until it was open, and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrow that protruded; then I introduced the corrosive medicine into the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became visible to me; and more than four months had passed when the wound began to heal, so I inserted forceps, from one side and the other, but they could not exit; therefore, I did not stop trying and devising various methods of instruments, until I took it out with well-made forceps on a certain day, as its shape will appear at the end of this chapter, and I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the surgeons deemed that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was fully cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the nature of extracting certain arrows, so that you may attend to what I do not say, for a book cannot comprehend everything; but the wise master compares little by little, and finds new work and nine tools for descending on strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not exit from the members where they are embedded except in two ways: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which exits at the same place it entered is an arrow embedded in flesh, and exits at times.[
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is rotted around it, and the abscess is eased; and similarly, if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, carefully cut around until the entire hole is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone, reaching one of the cerebral ventricles, and any of the mentioned accidents happen to the patient: do not pull it out, but let it be until it becomes even after several days, because if the arrow reaches the brain, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone, and does not reach up to the joint, and the patient remains for several days without any bad accident, then pull out the arrow.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply a styptic around, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the whole wound; and if you feel it, pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, widen the wound until it is large; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears or some other part holding it in place, remove the flesh that is stuck to it from both sides as much as you can, then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and take care not to break the arrow, but rather to pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out in one stroke, leave it there until the area around it softens, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is unfavorable, moderate what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use technique to gently remove the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or carefully; and place the patient in the same position he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him as the symptoms indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 For an arrow that comes from another direction, where something is visible or the skin is swollen in appearance: then cut there, as much as the forceps can grasp, and then extract it; but be careful not to injure further.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand circularly until it enters the bone and expands the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, let it remain, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the arrowhead is stuck in there, push the whole shaft in; and if it has fallen out, and you see that a wound has been created, administer cauterization, then introduce the slender instrument so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then pull it out, and if the arrowhead is stuck, introduce the slender instrument with the point entering in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the wound is contaminated, it is necessary to cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls in the foot or the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it, do so; and be careful not to cover the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows resembles a bird's beak, and see the shape here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the arrowhead is similar to the feather of a bird, for embedding in the tip of an arrow, as shown in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of forceps for putting in and pulling out, as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins of the common body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 Of the veins from which one bleeds are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen at the head, namely: two that are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples; and two veins that are in the eye socket of the two eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the tip of the nose; and the two tendons that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly bled are five in each arm: the one is called the "cephalic" and is located on the left side, and the lay people call it "head vein"; the middle one is called "faste", and it is made up of the cephalic and basilic, and the lay people call it "heart vein"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the lay people call it "belly vein", and it is above the fascia, and it is the one that is bled, which is clearly visible on the bulge.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the little finger and ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is located under the arch of the bulge on the left side, and the second saphena is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The sinews of veins that are behind the ears help against old catarrh and headache;
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The sinings of the two arteries that are in the temples are beneficial for old and sudden headaches, and customary eye inflammation, and watery eyes; and the qualities of the sining are as I tell you: and it is that the patient strains their neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your finger, and then stop the flow; then raise the skin above the vein up to your index finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and cut it as you did with the other veins, and let out the blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The bleeding of the frontal vein is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic in diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness; and its quality is such that the patient wrenches their neck while twisting, so that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the tip on the vein, and strike it with your hand or another object, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp and crooked because the bone is close, and there is a risk that the flame will break when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in the inner corners of the eyes helps with the eyes, and with itching, and with redness, and with inflammation in the eye, and with diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient wrenches their neck while twisting from some ligament, as before; then bleed, and let the incision be a little long and wide with the flame, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is too fine, it may break; then apply cauterization of blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The bloodletting from the vein of the nose is worthwhile for a quartan fever, and for a violent madness, and for diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, and even when it is old; and the qualities of the bloodletting are such that the patient constricts his neck, then constricts his nose with your left hand, and takes a slender flame long, and sticks it between the upper lip in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open widely, and the blood will begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the method of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The scarification of the two sinews helps with the narrowing of the windpipe, and the beginning of shortness of breath, and many diseases, and dropsy, and consumption, and scrofula, and herpes, and ulcers; and the quality of the scarification is such that the patient wrings his neck from under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the patient's head, and the patient sit on a chair, then open the vein of the long one a little widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then do the same thing in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and moderately tighten both veins, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until the morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the flow of pus from wounds (or abscesses)
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bloodletting from veins on the lips above can lead to chapped mouth, gum decay, lip cracks, and nasal congestion or swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the pus flow are as follows: make the patient sit in front of you and constrain their neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they can be recognized because they are black, and there are small black veins around them: cut then both, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, cut the largest one from each side; and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the pus flow under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The draining of veins that are under the tongue helps after the draining of the cephalic vein, and that is at the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and mouth illnesses; and the qualities of the one who drains are such that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks down on either side a black vein: then heal both and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 Veins of the knife with which one commonly purges are healed in two ways: either by puncturing with a large, mirten-wide flame, or with an olive-thin blade as a cutting knife, and it is called "anesil"; and [the knives] are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of a moderately wide flame is widely renowned and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary, for opening veins full of clotted blood visibly appearing, and containing thick and turbid blood; and this is the shape of the olive-colored flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed for cauterizing subtle veins, where there is thin yellow blood.[FAQ]
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed cautiously, and to be careful of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the flame should not be pricking, but cutting smoothly like a lancet.[https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/anesil](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/anesil)
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the vein does not open manifestly, you should constrict it, and apply another one; or seek a ramification of it, or heal the vein in place of it along the arm: it opens manifestly; and cover it with a dry cloth, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to recognize the location of the bleeding, you should proceed as follows: constrict the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and cover the vein with a dry cloth; and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the place swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it bulge up high, similar to a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is an artery wound: hasten then, and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; if the arm is injured, bind it and leave it so, and let the patient not move it; and be afraid, and let the patient not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it overpowers you, and the medicine is not at hand, cut the artery if it is visible, for its origin will retract, and stop the bleeding.[Note: This is a medieval medical treatment and may not be accurate or advisable according to modern medicine.].
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of fennel root, split it, and take one half of it and bind it on well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood flow; and stopping the bleeding is not difficult in many dispositions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's binding.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The wound from the vein let in milk, which helps it to heal; it draws blood both from the surface of the head and from the body underneath, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful near the nerve that is beneath, and if he punctures it too deeply, and finds the nerve, and it becomes inflamed and the wound becomes infected, and perhaps cannot be healed; and this nerve is often exposed, and if it is not exposed in some people due to its delicacy, then you must cure it with a blunt instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then you should cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The wound from the cephalic vein helps in drawing blood from the head and aiding the eyes; it is necessary to cure by pricking with an olive-colored or myrtle-colored flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because there are no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Nevertheless, one should try to find the most suitable position, and it is not a problem if you fail the first time, you can start again; and perhaps the area becomes swollen in some men when they fail the first time, but it is not a problem.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about venesection (bloodletting) is that it is not performed unless it is to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and the venesection should be done in one of the three veins, namely: cephalic, faste, and basilic; and one should perform venesection at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be performed on the first or third day, two or three days after.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The liquid that is administered for ailments has no set time, but rather when needed day or night, at all hours and in every moment; and one should not bleed children until the age of 14, nor pregnant women until the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And elderly people over the age of 60 should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when one wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they empty their bowels with a light enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw out impurities from the intestines causing harm to the principal members; nor should one bleed those who are overly full of food, or intoxicated, until they are sober, nor those who are dropsical; and one should not be bled after a colic, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent urination in women, work, staying awake and fasting, or any other cause that weakens the strength, either by weapon or by the body; then thin out the humors if the blood is thick by foods and drinks and medicines if you have them; then enter the bath if nothing prohibits it, to further thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the arm near the elbow as we have said; and on that day refrain from work, exertion, lust, and similar things; and be cheerful and joyous, and let the one who is bleeding raise their arm higher than the one performing the procedure, and rub their arm two or three times, then moderately tighten the ligature above the middle, for if it is too tight or loose, the blood will not flow; and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the bandage with a little oil, then place your left hand on the vein below the area to be bled, so that the vein does not move and slip away from the incision.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that run like the strings of a bow, and some are full of airiness, such that when placed on fire, they draw back from the flame and cannot be opened, and it is thus for these; and if one opens the vein, the wound will be too narrow. Therefore, the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it's good; if not, try again a little below or above the same place quickly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the limb is swollen and the patient is frightened, let him rest for one or two days and do not bind his arm, perhaps abscesses will form; do not enter into a bath, then resume the bloodletting if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows slowly and you fear that not enough blood will flow, then place the flame directly into that same hole; perform the procedure somewhat quickly, so that the limb remains swollen, for this occurs many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not begin the bleeding again, and put a little bit of oil lees on it, for it clears the body of blood, and the lees are sticky in this place like oil; and thus administer the lees of oil at every bleeding that you perform on the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and do the same with triacle and bole, when they are put on the swelling; the blood becomes subtle and spreads out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, even when it is only bled at that time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the place a wet sponge with warm water and salt, and hold it there for an hour; and you should do this after the issuing of blood from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains at the place after several days, it will not harm; and if you see it, put on something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in sage juice, marigold, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And it often happens that an abscess or discharge appears at the base of the penis; then place your hand on it, and if you find it soft upon pressure with your hand, this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be careful not to apply any of the things that we have mentioned, because it may happen that you pierce an artery; instead make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for one who is stout and robust, and in need of bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and let the wound be wide; and for the weak, do the contrary, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by piercing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And for one whose body needs bleeding, it is necessary to give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are feverish, bleed them three or four times; and if they have a cold complexion, feed them before the bleeding moist bread in muscat syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he has a fracture, after the loss of much blood, then he should eat broth of meat, and sweet-smelling syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm and purge himself otherwise, it is necessary, when he has become weakened by heavy bleeding, that he bleeds a little and often, according to the quantity of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if one wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he should bleed 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wants to purge himself elsewhere in the body, he should do so on the second day or the third.[NOTE: The word "lou" is an old French spelling of "le", meaning "the". It has been corrected for clarity.]
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood inside the body which is already heated and causes fever; therefore, a large quantity must be drawn and the wound opened wide until it can be closed with stitches; then ensure all conditions of fracture are met and place your hand on the pulse as the wound closes to prevent the patient from going into shock; this often happens when the surgeon is negligent. And when you release the arm and cause the blood to flow a second time, do not press firmly or forcefully if the wound has closed, but rather wait for it to close again; or use the point of a hot iron to melt the frozen blood clot at the opening of the vein and apply a cloth soaked in warm water, pressing lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not apply any pressure until the abscess has calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled at the elbow because it is larger and more complex.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of bleeding is as follows: the patient puts his hand in warm water until the veins become red; then it should be bound loosely, so that the vein can be seen clearly; then bleed him across, not lengthwise or widthwise; and make the incision large, and let it be bled close to the joint of the hand, and if pus cannot come out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if this is done in the summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is used more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than any other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The sap of the salvation plant of the right hand is worthwhile for all liver diseases, and this is how: straighten the hand, and immerse it in hot water, until the vein fills up, if one sees it; and if the sap flows crooked, and if you cut it completely from every side, it does not matter; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath entirely stripped of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as is necessary, then put oil and wax on the vein to quickly heal it, and do the same for every wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The letting of blood from the left hand is beneficial to disease in the right side of the body, and you should do as I have told you for the right side.[INTRODUCING THE INPUT FORMAT:
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The sap of the sopshen plant is worthwhile for all illnesses that are below the body, such as diseases of the intestines, retention of gases, and illnesses of the kidneys, thighs, and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the qualities of his bleeding are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it disappears, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from there over the foot go many veins; bleed therefore at the largest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is easier.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and cut the flesh crosswise as in slicing; and let the flame be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if blood cannot come out, put the foot in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the bleeding fails the first time, try again a little higher up, for the place is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the shin of the other leg as well.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of fire, and its bleeding is worth for the pain of inflammation, when it's because of hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the qualities of his bleeding are such that the patient enters the bath and squeezes above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, bleed in all ways that you can, and crossing; and it is better to cut it than to let it continue, for the place is dry, and it is very deep in some men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't find it there, seek a vein of it that is visible on the back of the leg, and toward the small toe, and beware of nerves; and make the blood flow until you see, and then loosen the ligature and put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 ventouse sanities/blisters
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and vacuum therapy is performed in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking (i.e., without breaking the skin).
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this ventosation, which is without striking, is of two kinds: either it is entirely with heat, or without heat; and ventosation made by striking and bloodletting is done in fourteen parts of the body, one of which is right at the top of the head; another is in the middle of the neck; and two are on the two sides of the neck; and one under the chin; and one on each of the two shoulders; and one on the haunches; and one between the two arms; and one on each of the two legs; and one on each of the two ankles; and this ventosation does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken at all, as one does with venesection; and it should not be administered, either with or without heat, in any disease that comes from plethora, until the whole body is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to cupping, or for customary purposes, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in-between and at every time; for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkening of the eyes; and there are such who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and ooze blood; and there are some who dream, and see through night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and likewise when it is mid-month, we recommend that they be bled after three hours of daylight.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The letting of blood from the nose helps with a crack in the head that comes to the eyes, and it is not appropriate for it to be after the evacuation of the entire body; and this cupping is in place of the letting of blood from the head, and it is not appropriate for those of cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, because it harms them greatly; and for this reason, old people should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who frequently use it often become forgetful, and so one should place the cup slightly lower out of caution for forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventilation to the neck is located near the artery of the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason, it is useful for constriction of the nipple, and fissure of the channel of the throat, and in all cases, and in repletion; and it should be used sparingly, because if it stays too tightly, it can cause oblivion or stomach and heart ailment.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventilation between the two ribs of the neck is useful for headaches, eye diseases and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is located near the basilic vein; and you must instruct the surgeon to press lightly when placing his hand, so as not to cut the artery and cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The pains from windy biles under the chin are equivalent to diseases of the mouth, and decay of the gums, and similar illnesses that exist in the mouth; and it is located in the area of the swelling of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The pains from windy biles in the shoulders are equivalent to illnesses that come from heat and overfilling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 Wounds of the thigh are as valuable as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and it advises the physician not to strike too deep, for the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the buttocks is beneficial for hemorrhoids of the anus and for diseases beneath, and it must be large and made of iron because it needs to draw well; and perhaps if it were too fine, it would break and cause great wounds.[Oriental Medicine: Cupping Therapy](https://www.healthcmi.com/Acupuncture-Continuing-Education-Classes/1480-oriental-medicine-cupping-therapy)
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs heal openly because they draw blood from throughout the body and are beneficial for old pains in the joints, gout, and bladder, and they resolve inflammation; they are placed on the shins and ankles, but even so, they weaken the body after long use and cause paralysis in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying cupping glasses is as follows: place it empty first and then fill it gradually with suction; do this quickly and move it around, not stopping until you see the area turn red and swell, and observe the appearance of blood; then strike it and replace the cups, paying attention to the condition of the body because some people have dry skin and clear pores: for such individuals, strike only once and make wide, shallow incisions that are not too deep; and apply gentle suction.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw little by little, one time is sufficient.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want much blood, let us apply the cups frequently; and if the blood is thick, strike deep, and the goal is to quickly pierce the heart; and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with warming and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of cucurbit seed; and if it is in winter, with oil of watercress, lily, chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of costmary, or oil of dill, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed with water after ventosation (the act of exposing a wound to air) of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have an abundance of moisture, (it is recommended to) rise with ease, or with water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.[STT: For people with a lot of moistness, it's suggested to get up with water that contains myrtle, sumac, and similar ingredients.]
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have excessive wetness get up from old wine, or dry water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar; and one should not be bled with a cup before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and one should not sleep after the ventosation (the act of exposing a wound to air), and it is necessary that they stay awake when they are about to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And beware if the one who is healing is of a choleric temperament, and if their blood is too thick and inflamed; they should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at ease, and similar things; and eat chicken broth, and meat from mutton, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And let the one with a cold complexion take honey syrup, and middle-aged scented wine, which is between old and new, and eat pork, and chicken and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they are to be bled, they should drink more than they eat; and it is appropriate to give some people triacle or muscat before or after the bleeding, to comfort the principal members; and let their blood be thinned, but it is not at all suitable for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 Cups that are placed without striking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and abscesses and legs and inflammation, because these members cannot withstand being struck, and one does not do it except to draw blood from member to member, as we place on the breasts when the milk is healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the stomach and on the abscesses to reduce the member; and to remove pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, such that it removes the obstruction by its attractive power, or dislodges the stone from its place; and it does this when one places it on the liver and on the spleen when there is trapped wind, and these cups are administered empty to only suck; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in pleurisy diseases, and in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water, or with water in which suitable herbs for this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of applying the cupping cup with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and have on the side near the middle a small hole, as big as to put a needle through, and be made of brass, smooth before so that it does not prick the patient when placed on the member; and have in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron, to hold a candle in place, and let there be both large and small [blisters/suction cups], according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for the blisters/suction cups of children are different than those of the elderly, and of the thin compared to those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And one should place this blister/suction cup on the member in such a way: apply the candle of wax or linen, and put it across the crossbar that is inside the blister/suction cup, so that the flame reaches the bottom of the blister/suction cup but does not burn the patient; then place it on the member, with your fingers over the hole that we mentioned, so that when you want, the vapor can come out and the blister/suction cup can be removed; then reapply the linen as before, and repeat frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the cup which is applied in disease of pleurisy, it has no rod or opening, and it is applied only when it is full of water, and is placed on the body part; and this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Blisters are applied only to parts of the body where cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare areas of flesh, such as fingers or nose, and others; and the quality of the blisters is that when you find blisters that are in clear, sweet water without putrefaction, then take them; and place one in clean, fresh water until they become familiar (acclimated), and have nothing in their bellies; and then they should be let by bloodletting and cupping, then rub the member until it becomes red, and place the blisters on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a cup can be placed, then place one, for this is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the swelling of the hip, and then of water, very well, and then bind it; and if the swelling remains too long after the body of the veins, wet a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is multiplied, put crushed vitriol, or alum, and similar things on it, until it subsides; or you put half of peeled beans on the swelling, and leave them until they dry on the swelling, it will stop now; and if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the veins will not swell, rub the swelling with fresh blood, or insert a needle until blood comes out, and then place them on it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they are slackening, powder some crushed aloe and salt, or ash, on them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that foolish doctors throw away this chapter, as they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read letters; and for this reason, knowledge is estranged in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except through the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have extracted the knowledge, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is appropriate that we mention in the prologue of this book the summary of the teachings and the chapters in which the wise person focuses their attention and dwells on the truth, so that those who have been tested may know and learn this noble art, and then teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or breakage comes to anyone, one must quickly heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or infants, or the elderly; or if the time is not extremely hot, or very cold; and eat dry foods, that is to say cold meats, and bird and roe deer meat, and do not drink wine, or eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are certain of a hot abscess, or spreading of matter to the limb; so that the patient returns to their usual regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make for thick nourishment, such as wheat boiled in water, and rice, and meat, and dairy, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the body regains strength and the break heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or join together properly according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, nor can those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children. But it doesn't matter, reset the broken bone and use large tongs that hold and bring the limb together until it heals as it was before; and do not disturb its work, and for this reason, you must feed it hearty foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a skull fracture is different than a rib fracture or a leg fracture, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
