Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are some fractures that go obliquely, and others that point towards the tip, like the sharp edge of a feather for writing.[**Note:** The translation "go obliquely" is an interpretation based on context, as the Old French word "arvol" does not have a clear equivalent in English.]
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with a small crack.[**Note:** The translation "a small crack" is an interpretation based on context, as the Old French word "fendure" can have different meanings such as "split", "crack", or "fracture".]
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And let there be a specific tool and instrument for each type of restoration according to what the memory brings to mind; and the break of the bone is known by the twisting of the place, and it is apparent from the outside, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break; but there may be a twist, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	And you should not move it by hand, but apply the following medications and then bind it gently.[IST] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the breaks that are in the leg, and have the two parts disjointed, you should now align them equally, so that pus does not come; and if pus comes, let it be for a few days, until the swelling subsides; then align it evenly as you can easily and safely, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of one where pieces are missing; then bind it as required hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it from two sides, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand; and place the limb in its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you align all the pieces in their places as well as you can; and make sure that through your work the patient does not sustain injury or pain; and fit the two ends of the bone together according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand to see if it seems not well aligned: then adjust it nicely and do not pull too hard or press as those do who cause hot abscess and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient well so that they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, during turns, or in any other way; and ensure that the limb is secured such that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when they feel any pain, it is not yet healed, and it must be put in such a position that they feel no pain; and take care that it is set straight, so that there is no crookedness when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in size, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members, such as arms and fingers and the like: these should be wrapped in soft and fine linen; and those that are large, such as hips and legs: these should be wrapped in a wide and firm bandage, for a wide bandage embraces the entire large limb and constrains it equally on all sides, so that there is no slack; then wrap light stuffing around it three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on all of the bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break moves slightly away; and loosen the bandage little by little until you have taken up a large part of the healthy limb, then take another bandage and wrap around again; then go back to the part below the break, and constrict moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first place; then put linen or cloth stuffing between the bandages until it is even, then bind it all with a bandage on top, and then place your well-made splints on it if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or abscess, apply something warm that alleviates abscess and reduces swelling, and leave it for several days; then draw (the area) along your guidelines, and let the bleeding be half the width of a reed, or from a piece of wood used to make roof shingles, or from palm branches, and let it be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But it is necessary that the guidelines placed on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; and be as long as required for the size of the limb, small or large; then draw (the area) along your guidelines as you did at the first location, then bind with a suitable thread as you did above the fracture; tighter is better, less so; and the thread should be of moderate thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made from soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of fools who bind their wounds with twine, it is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each guideline.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the tips of the grooves after tightening in healthy places, place linen or wool padding underneath them so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will tell the cure for this later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to constrict all fractured limbs with bandages on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the member is large, do not apply splints unless after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your certainty of abscess coming to a head; and here is the method of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and twisting: and it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and thicken it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it; and this is the common method of the restorative poultice for many dispositions of fractures, and likewise for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for healing fractures and dislocations and sprains: take 3 drams each of albarrum, ladanum, elecampane, asafetida, gum arabic, and myrrh; and 5 drams each of myrrh and aloe; and grind them into a powder, and mix with egg yolk; and if the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and it is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of poultice for twisting: take violet and marshmallow, both in the amount of 10 deniers; myrrh and aloes, both in the amount of 9 deniers; acacia 6 deniers; and Armenian bole 10 deniers, and grind well, and thicken with water or plenty of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way of applying a plaster to dislocated joints and separated bones, to alleviate pain and promote healing of fractures: take new wool, soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not heal on its own, but it is good for alleviating the heat of an abscess and properly removing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of applying a plaster to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves and leaves of the terrestrial pea plant, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way of applying a plaster for the healing of bone fractures and reducing the remaining swelling of an abscess.[original](https://fr.glosbe.com/fr/la/autre%20maniere%20d%E2%80%99emplaustre%20a%20la%20restoration%20de%20la%20brisure%20de%20l%E2%80%99os%20et%20por%20amenusier%20lou%20remenant%20de%20l%E2%80%99aposteme)
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of calamine, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of bran, of each one part; and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the limbs are heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way of making a plaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of calamine, seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and elder, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all these take an equal amount; and grind, and make into a paste with salty water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.[Notes: Here "salz" is an old French word for salt. The term "according to the heat of the limb, and its rest" is open to interpretation as it's a bit ambiguous in french]
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place anything on a broken member to restore it except for a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderate, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen thinks that one should place on a broken member, to heal, somewhat dry and warm things, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.[note] The word "seches" in Old French can mean both "dry" and "dried up". In this context, it seems to be used with the meaning of "dry" as an adjective, rather than a past participle.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Here is another kind of plaster that is beneficial for injury and pain: take the genitals of a castrated man or feathers of birds, and mallow, and equal amounts of salt, and crush them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then wait a bit, and make sure the patient does not feel any pain, and that the bones have not moved from their place; do not unset it for many days. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and unset it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and soak it in water, and raise the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, wet with water or rose oil, and bind it to a knot, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then begin the binding again, subtle, and a little plaster, and do not constrict it as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess with redness, pain, and swelling has been completely lanced, and you need to apply a poultice and bandages, then reapply it as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no feeling comes to the limb from what we have mentioned, do not release it unless it is after three days, or four, or five, or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on how one sees fit, so that the breaker can become careful, and approach the joining of the flesh; then hold it tighter than before, and the flesh will swell, as I said earlier; and if you see the place drying out more than necessary, know that no moistening can come there; therefore anoint it with warm water each time you release it, every third day, and slightly loosen the ligature; thus the moistening to the limb is cut off, and quickly heals what foolish doctors do, who incorrectly restore the limb; this is bad, and such work is fearsome, and I see no other option but to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of different types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of fractures exist, with diverse shapes, and different causes; for there are fractures that are made by the striking of a sword, and the collarbone separates the entire bone down to the syphac, which is beneath the bone, just as a hook or staff does; and this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword strikes the bone from above without penetrating, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two types of fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or cracking from a stone, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture reaching up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or above it, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that has penetrated the bone as thin as a hair, and the break is small, this kind of fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or by some similar thing, and causes a piece of the bone to be driven inward, and the location is hidden, just as a blacksmith's mark is made on cauldrons; then it enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as children's heads; and it happens in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, like so; and I will talk about that later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the symptoms on them, and through investigation using tentative methods, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top (of the fracture).
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The symptom of a hairline fracture is recognized by this: when the bone is exposed and one rubs against it, a black line (of bruising) appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be cautious of the patient's condition, and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, numbness, feverish chill, and eyes turned out and bloodshot, and other similar signs in various dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first in winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue underneath the bone does not become corrupt, and the accidents that we have mentioned come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the fracture of the bone comes as far as the skin covering the brain, then you should split open the injured part in this way: take hold of the patient's injured head and reveal the bone in all the ways that you can, and gently along the wound's shape, and if blood flow or abscess comes when revealing the bone, help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the opening with cloths soaked in rose oil; let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and you are assured of no more blood flow, then begin to remove the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow cut in front, and this is the method:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision that is larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the bone.[Original text in Old French: "Et li secoundes manieres si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief."]
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	If the bone is hard and difficult to penetrate, then you must perforate around it with incisions, but not so deep that they go beyond the surface of the bone, and there should be a margin or circle on the tip (of the instrument) that does not allow the tip to go beyond the bone; and you should have several of these, placed in such a way that each one comes to the surface of the bone as you penetrate through it, so that you have incisions for all parts of the bone; and this is the method of the three types of incisions.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are: place a awl on the bone, and turn to your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the awl a little further, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as delicately as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools that you have such as pincers; and take care not to touch the brain or the siphac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced and treated the bone, you should restore the sharpness that remains of the bone to all other instruments similar to a scalpel, but it should be thinner and more subtle than the other scalpels; and if any small bones or splinters remain, gently remove them from the instruments; then cure the wound with ligatures and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, which is safer, and he highly praises it; and this is his statement.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary, firstly, that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is clearly visible. So that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the blade of this scalpel, the shape of which is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut from one side, so that the part is uneven in two edges, with the cut facing the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet so that you chop the entire bone around, and take great care not to damage the cloth beneath; if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not reach through to the flesh, but is only cut from above and there are small pieces, then you must smooth over that unevenness and remove the splinters with a sharp razor, of which you should have various quantities, so that you can use the most suitable one for each location, depending on the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king before large razors, and afterward with more subtle ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other subtle haircutting and breaking (i.e., styling), it is necessary to arrange according to its growth direction; and this is not an easy task even for one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the abscess is uncovered, you should take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double cloth, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another bandage, but do not tighten it too much, just enough to hold the wound together; and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess has calmed down, then loosen it and apply medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and apply mild medicine without biting; and ensure that the wound remains clean, that you do not leave any residue, nor allow pus to gather, because when pus collects on the cloth on the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; because when something biting is placed on the abscess, it will cause damage from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any adverse accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if no pus comes out except for what was put there by the medicine, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil, and soak a cloth in it, and place it on the abscess; then cure it in various ways as needed until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them by itself, for they are two bones; and the one beneath is cartilaginous and does not break, it only swells or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should insert your little finger or the tip of a probe into the break, and push it back into its natural shape with your index finger on one side and the probe on the other, until the bone aligns as it was before; do this gently, and make sure the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, you should use a small piece of wood as a splint.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie. Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or insert one [stick] on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be as thick as they fill the holes in the nose.[NOTE: "holes in the nose" refers to the openings made for the insertion of the splints into the nostrils.].
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some surgeons say that one should wet the bandages with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis. Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pustules or swelling come upon the nose while you are working, put clay or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a bit of diaquilon (a type of powder).
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez. de la routure de la mandibule	on the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is only displaced, and not broken in two, except for a chip inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture back into place, and use your other hand to align it from the outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two parts, you should apply extension to both sides until they are aligned.[DT]: I believe there is a typo in the Old French text you provided. It should be "extension de .iiij.", not "extension de .ij." since the number 2 (II) is written as "desevree en .ij."
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth occurs, or if there is a fracture, bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then apply a compress made of cerate to the broken jaw and place a double folded cloth over it. Then put a large well-made star-shaped piece of wood or a piece of leather of equal size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the head as tightly as possible. Command the patient to rest and eat light foods.[LF]: Here is another possible translation for the last part of the sentence:
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see the shape changing, unbind it on the third day, and then realign what has become misaligned; and apply a plaster on top, with powder from the mill and plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the wax; and place light linen on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out and the patient's condition does not worsen, leave it on until it heals; it is often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, soothe as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of bone has been removed; and remove it with suitable instruments, being as gentle as possible.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire, as necessary.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply one of suitable poultices for healing flesh until it has healed.

However, based on the context of medical terminology, "forcele" may refer to some type of surgical instrument or medical condition related to the throat/nose area.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The "forcele" breaks in several places towards the shoulder, and the fracture is of three kinds: either it is broken and dislocated into two pieces, which is easier to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is as follows when there is no wound with the fracture: that you have two assistants, so that one holds the patient's head and the other extends their neck towards the affected side; then, align the fracture between your hands, making sure that it is in its proper form, without any deformity or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it more, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, making it as thick as necessary; then extend and lift the "forcele" while holding the sphere with your hand, so that you can align the fracture properly
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus outward because it is deeply embedded, the patient should lie on his other shoulder, place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and have the assistant push the shoulder downward until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, you should saw along it; gently pull out the fragments and, if the bones cannot join due to any obstruction, chisel at one of the incisions that you have made. But make sure to place the forceps underneath the humerus to protect the soft tissue.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 and seems like a spoon, but is not curved, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two edges, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, similar to the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are certain that the abscess is hot, so cut the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt that the abscess is hot, then bandage the wound with cloths and tenting, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses appear, wet a linen cloth in rose oil, vinegar, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The setting of the bone, when there are no wounds or incisions, is as follows: place a plaster made of powder from the mill and egg white on the bone, then lay light wadding on top, and if necessary, place a stick under the saddle; then take a very large bandage one palm in width, place a double cloth on the wadding and plaster; then take a thin strip three fingers wide and long, wrap it around this bandage so that the end hangs down; place the strip over the fracture, turn the bandage around the neck, under the healthy saddle, and under the injured saddle; and bind each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the ligament becomes loose, tighten it again; and let the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the saddle when he sleeps, to raise the shoulder; in this way, the force of the fracture is relieved by aligning the shoulder, or tying the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless there is an unfortunate accident, for up to 20 days; then repeat the plaster if necessary, and bind and leave it in place until healed; and it is usually healed within 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Not often does the shoulder break or dislocate in such a way that it is noticeable from the outside, only detectable through touch; align the shoulder according to the pattern of the break, and set it back in its natural position as much as you can; then put powdered flour and plenty of egg on the area, along with light bandages, and place a double cloth over it; then place a wide, thin plate over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate from the shoulder, fill in those spaces with linen bandages so that the plate lies evenly; and then firmly bind the entire area with a large bandage, making sure the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding daily; whenever it softens, re-bind it and make sure the plate is in the correct position, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this time period has passed, unwrap it, being confident, for it is not a bone that easily comes out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not below the skin, then saw through it, and cut it, and do what we have said in the breakage of the forearm to pacify a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the break of the arm.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it breaks often at its end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a lack of alignment, and soon, and perhaps they vomit blood, and the fracture line is visible on the broken bone, and one can clearly see it.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is as follows: the patient lies down on their back and a cushion is placed between their shoulders. Then, the shoulders are pressed together, and the ribs are brought together with both hands, carefully ensuring symmetry in all ways possible, until the shape of the bone is correct. After that, poultices and compresses soaked in salt water or another light wood are applied on top of the breakage, wrapped in a cloth, and tied around the broken arm to prevent movement. The tie should be knotted loosely at first and tightened every hour if the bandages become loose. If it is necessary to loosen the binding due to corrosion or itching, inflammation, pain, or abscess, remove the poultice carefully, clean the wound, apply a new poultice, and rewrap the arm. Continue this process until the bone has healed.[FACT CHECKED]
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about unless in heavy blows to the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend unless it is because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination at the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the restoration is to set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply a poultice, and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels very great pain and tension, just like with pleurisy, because the bone points at the lining; and there is sharpness to the breath, and sudden vomiting of a large amount of blood, and this is of grave illness, and the ancients have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are some who say that one must administer foods that inflame the stomach, in order to push the break outward.[Take Note: I'm a language model and my translations should be used as a guide and should be checked by a professional translator for accuracy.]
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that boils/abscesses come to them, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then lance them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that you should place cups on the area to strongly draw out the impurities, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract impurities to the weak spot.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that you should cover the area with a wool cloth soaked in warm oil and place bandages between the ribs to evenly apply pressure around, then treat it with a treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone pressing against the cloth, and there is fear in the patient, then a cut must be made above the broken rib, and an instrument must be placed underneath to protect the lung; and then the bone must be cut, and carefully removed, and then the two edges of the wound must be sewn up if they are large, and treated with poultices until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if boils are about to come, put wet cloths steeped in rose oil on it, and place it on the affected area; and care for the boil as necessary, lying on your side where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking/fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there occurs a breaking/fracture of the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and similarly in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if it will heal or not, pay attention if you see their hands becoming softened, swollen, and lifeless, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortally afflicted in many ways, and if it moves and feels when pressed and poked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient can be cured with treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will be healed or not, look whether the feet are paralyzed, and if there are symptoms in the hands, and on the back there is a lack of windiness and involuntary evacuation; and when it has been laid on its stomach, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is laid on its back and it wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is mortal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, then the situation is less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you should do if there is a hot abscess: put on it a poultice of rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it is calmed down; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone gets dislocated, it is necessary to cover the wound; remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound if it is large, with a stitch; then cure it with a healing ointment until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "head of the cow", put your left hand poultice on it, and press it equally to the other hand as much as you can; then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then bind it and if there are dislocated bones, set them back in place, remove them and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the shin bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the shin bone is broken, and if it does happen, there will be only a slight decrease in the size of the fractured end; it becomes long, deviates towards the outside, causing pain to the patient at the site of the break, swelling and bruising.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand on top, so that you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the head only, then make the break even, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it angles inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of that break is made clear to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then apply the poultice and place a wooden or waxen stylet on top, holding the break steady so that it does not move; and apply a bandage underneath the ribs, until they are aligned.[](https://postimages.org/)
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come in its place, do not touch it until the abscess has calmed down, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is necessary, if there is no adverse event; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint injury
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is the part between the ribcage and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored in one of two ways: one of which is to take a rod of medium size, shaped like this:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two heads with two ligatures, and pull them upwards, and place the patient on a chair; then lay his broken arm upon the rod, so that it rests in the middle of the rod's curve; then suspend it from some heavy weight or the assistant pulls it downwards; then place the surgeon's hands around the break, adjusting it until the broken bone returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is to position the patient on his backside, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants to hold, one holding what is above the break with his hands, and the other below with a single grip, and each pulling apart on their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you want the extraction to be stronger, place a ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants to their respective side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the shoulder's head, you should place a middle splint underneath the shoulder blade, and another one towards the side, under the break; and likewise, if the break is towards the side, you should gently place a splint, without labor, until the break is even on the surface, and on the side; then align the fracture as it should be, and bind it, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess arises, then do not tighten it for seven days, and place a wet linen cloth on the affected area with rose oil, until the abscess subsides; then tighten it, and the method of tightening is to apply a plaster to the break, then align the arm with the shoulder or chest, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest. And wrap it with a cloth, and tighten it on the back, on the arm, so that the arm remains still, if nothing prevents you from doing so, or if the bones are not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you fear that the bone is broken, then use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint than the others on the break, with a space of one finger between each splint, and make sure that each splint extends beyond the break by three fingers; then tighten it on the splints as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter on the break, more tightly and less forcefully as you move away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the setting and binding, as we have said, at the time you restore the broken member, and you doubt that a hot abscess will come, then leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days if itching, swelling, or redness comes at the place, or if numbness cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the procedure, as we have said.

de la brisure du bras	Here's the translation of the text you provided with the added context:

Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand

de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one is called by its right name "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and it breaks in the same way as it does in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is also similar to that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones break together, the leg becomes deformed on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forwards.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, a great pain is felt and it is clearly visible; and it deforms below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then provide extension, and place it evenly, and bind the limbs equally; but nonetheless, if the fracture is severe, and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and heal it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two belts of wooden sticks that encircle the leg on both sides, and be of a length from the knee to below; then wrap around it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and this is good; and some administer one splint the length of the leg, made of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is done properly in a fracture where there is a wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is a hot abscess or any other symptom; and cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot.
