de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Here is a translation of the previous text with added information about the specific injury:
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the woman's pelvic bone is broken, make her sit with her legs spread apart, then lean her back and support it from behind; then fill the cavity of the patient's pelvis with cotton, as thick as a finger; then stand the woman up and lift her belly and lower back, and the cotton will come out of the opening until it reaches the broken bone, and the bone will return to its place along with the finger; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she is done, replace it, and do this for 7 days or so: the fracture will be healed. And if you wish, take a bladder of herbs, and attach a cane to its opening, and insert the entire bladder into the pelvis; then blow forcefully into the cane until the bladder is inflated inside: the broken bone will return to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the forearm in a man or woman is broken, it should be restored in the same way as we have said for the shinbone; and such shallow fractures are not hidden from one who applies their effort and skill, and pays attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the break indicates in several ways the correct path of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap it with bandages and leave it for three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of a fracture with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder blade or similar, that it be healed now, as the wounds that we mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, apply vitriol to it, if you have none other thing, and then begin again to set the fracture in that same hour, or on that same day, unless abscesses come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses do come there, then leave the setting of the fracture until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed down, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad outcome to occur.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the fractured bone is apparent on the surface of the skin, then it is necessary to carefully and gently align it with your hands, using light pressure.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not ready for you to place evenly in your hands, then realign it with this instrument that is made of iron, which is 7 or 8 fingers long, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to press down with 3 or 4 fingers, depending on what is needed in each fracture repair; and it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the limb while you are working, and it should be sharp in front, and thick from the middle going forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," which means that the curved part must be placed on top of the visible end of the bone; and push it once until it aligns, so that they are even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is fine, and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut the end of the bone until the instrument has enough power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument for this purpose, such as a knife or scalpel, to the best of your ability; and scrape away the roughness and small shards that remain in the bone.[translated by user-981653874]
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient still feels great pain, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Make sure it is back in its place, then wet a cloth in black stiptic wine, and apply it properly if it is summer; and do not put any plaster or anything with oil on the wound, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer painkillers when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cutting away the covering to fit the size of the wound, taking care that the wound is not constricted by the break; many foolish surgeons have made this mistake, causing the patient either death or corruption; and let the restraints be softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or severe, and you fear that harm may come (to it), as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then soft wraps should not be placed on it; instead, use hard bandages and bind them in place of the soft ones.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one or two days that pus is forming on the wound, remove what you have placed on it and apply a healing salve, such as the four-ingredient ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it has healed and become whole.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be bandaged in such a way that the swelling can easily flow downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but instead keeps swelling up again, know that there are small fragments of bone in it, which is why you must probe the wound with a tent and remove all the loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then you must treat it according to what is described in its chapter earlier on.[Translation notes: "fistule" is an abnormal tube-like passage from a hollow organ to the body surface, and "corruption" refers to rotting or decay. The text likely means that if there is any sign of infection or further complication, the physician should refer to an appropriate chapter for treatment.]
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and visible on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, do not pull it out, for often death results; but leave it alone until it rots; perhaps it will come out by itself after twenty or thirty days; then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of boils that appear on the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see after the healing of the fracture, even when it is close to the joint, and it is ugly to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take notice then if the swelling is fresh: and administer styptic medicines to it, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, in such a way that you take one of these things, or all together, and cook them with a styptic wine or with egg yolk or with vinegar; and put it on the wound in rags, and bind it well, and do not unbind it for several days; and then undo it, and begin another, until the swelling is gone; or bind it to a piece of wood that is well made; for the property of wood is such that it removes all inflammations from the members; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off and let the excess appear; or have it scraped by a skilled barber, until it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the weakened limb after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and delicate afterward, it happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the nutrients could not reach the limb; or due to an excess of pus; or due to excessive movement at the wrong time; or because there is little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is for you to make the patient eat, and make the body supple, so that blood may multiply within him; and administer baths, and give joy and pleasure; then apply poultices on the limb, so that the poultice draws a large amount of nutrients to it, and often moisten it with warm water, until the nutrients reach the limb; and the limb returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the crooked limb after health has been restored
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is crooked after restoration, and the bone is visibly broken, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, it does not mean that it has lost its natural function; do not believe those who say that the limb should be broken again, for many foolish surgeons have done this in our land; and such works are to be blamed, leading to great harm, and perhaps even death; however, if the nodules and twisting are fresh, they must be soaked with warm water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as vismalve leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things; and make a softening ointment, such as a well-made dyaquilon, and take marsh mallow juice, and cook it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply the ointment; or use fat figs, and crush them with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes nodes are removed by continuous and lengthy rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And move the limb every hour to keep it supple.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted parts (tortuositez) are swollen and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then one must cut (cover) it down to the bone, using a sharp, light incision; and place a bandage and splint on the wound for treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	A dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it should be corrected immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if you wait, the area swells, and it may be difficult to reset; therefore, do not move it when it is swollen, for this often causes spasms and other pains; however, when this occurs, let the patient take a laxative, then leave him alone until the abscess has subsided; then soak the limb in warm water and oil and gently reset it, treating each limb as needed.[NOTE: I am not sure what "let the patient take a laxative" means in this context. It could also mean to make the patient vomit or purge him in some other way.]
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaw[https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandible](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandible)
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that both jaws are dislocated, and there are two ways of their dislocation: either they are slightly out of place and a bit loose; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chin, with saliva flowing from the mouth that he cannot hold, and cannot close his mouth, and his tongue is trapped by his speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return to its place through several methods.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is intact and complete, you must quickly reset it and not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places his small pillow (or mirepoix) of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and let the other hand be free to align (or make equal); and command the patient to relax, his jawbones, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the doctor places it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the returning is difficult, even if it is the two jawbones together, soak them in hot water and oil, until they are easily reset; do not delay the resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are equally reset, and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, place wet bandages (or compresses) on the wound, made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft ligaments; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his head resting between two cushions so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor strive to chew, but eat light food until the pain is gone and the jawbones are healed; and then eat whatever he wants lightly, and do not struggle to open his mouth while eating and drinking, until the jawbones are well healed and cured.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be set right within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fevers and habitual hiccups will ensue, and perhaps abdominal bloating, and possibly vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a lost cause; and many times, the one for whom it happens will die within 9 days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot be removed from the side of the ribs continuously and from the breast, and is sometimes removed in error, which can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is as follows: let the patient lie flat on their back, and extend their arms; and then press firmly with your palm on the area, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it; and the hip that is dislocated towards the leg cannot come out of place; unless it does, and if it dislocates at any time, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly, the hip is put back in its place when it is dislocated from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder[SR1] \*
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder does not dislocate in any other way than according to three manners: one of which is when it dislocates at the side towards the hip; and the second is towards the armpit; and perhaps it dislocates towards the top, but this is rare; and it never dislocates backwards towards the shoulder blade, nor inwards towards the nerves; and more often than not, it dislocates downwards towards the hip, especially in those who have little flesh, for it slips quickly in them; in those who have enough flesh, it slips less and returns less easily.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men, a strike or a break, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should examine it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known as a dislocation when it is lowered towards the shoulder blade, and it creates a distinction between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and below the shoulder blade where you touch the top of the shoulder, just like an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor move at all; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly when you touch; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to set back in place, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the caregiver to lift the patient's hand upwards, then place their fingers underneath the armpit and forcefully lift the joint upwards to its proper place. The caregiver should then lift the arm further upwards, place it back down, and do this repeatedly until it returns quickly to its original position.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come back as we have said in many days, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and a soothing and softening poultice should be applied, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and it should be applied; then the patient should be propped up on his back, and a woolen pad equal in size, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed below the shoulder blade; then have the patient place his heel on the pad, and lift the healthy shoulder forcefully, and pull the sick person's hand; and let another servant hold the patient's head so that it does not move downward; this shoulder will return immediately if you see it being set back in this manner: and this is to have a person present who is larger than the patient; and stand facing his side, and place his shoulder under the sick person's armpit, and lift the armpit upward, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another servant pulls the sick person's hand down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, have them carry something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the dislocation is also reset in another way: it involves sticking a long stake into the ground so that the patient's head rests on it like a pillow, and it should not be too thick or too thin; then place it under the patient, but make sure they have soft blankets over them, and the patient should lie still with their hand stretched out away from their body; then the joint will quickly return to its place; and if it does not wish to return despite all these things that we have mentioned, perform this treatment: take a stake of two arms in length and four fingers in width, which has a pointed end to enter deeply beneath the socket, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then place a soft cloth over the stick, so that the stick does not hurt or wound the patient, and place it beneath the dislocation of the patient; extend their arm along the length of the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on one step of a ladder of appropriate width, and let the hand hang down, leaving the body suspended on the other side: now the joint will return into place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, no matter how, you should then put a wool pad of equal size under the dislocation, then apply a poultice made with powdered flour, incense, and egg white, all over the shoulder and around it, then tie it down firmly under the dislocation, wrap the bandage back over the poultice, hold the patient's hand to their neck, and leave the hand in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they eat only soft food until the limb feels better, as this will aid in a faster recovery; and then they may eat more solid food after 5 or 7 days, and begin to move the limb; and if it feels firm and no longer swollen, then it has healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, you should apply cauteries to three openings, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint cannot hold and the arm cannot be raised upwards, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are to the side of the hip, or the breasts, or the back, are made by impact and extension of the hands, and another joint is used as a replacement; and it is treated until it has healed.[Literal translation] Dislocation which is toward the hip, and the breasts, or behind, is made by impulsion and extension of hands, and another joint is administered as a replacement; and one cures it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes cracking in the limb and difficulty in moving, then the patient should take many baths until this cracking is relieved and returns to its original state.[Literal translation] And if after the healing comes cracks to the member, and slowness in movement, then the patient uses bath many times, as much as that cracking is eased, and it returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; it is dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been put back in place, for it is clearly visible and can be felt; it is dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the cut patient with the flesh, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it should be reset in such a way that abscesses come to form there, for if abscesses were to form there, setting it back in place would be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be fully set back in place, especially when it is located in the back; this type of dislocation is worse than others, and causes more pain, and possibly death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration, when it is possible to set it back in place, is as follows: stretch out the patient's hand with both of your hands; and let their arms be extended, and have the doctor's hands around the rib, both above and below, and push the joint back into its place at its roots or at the base of the palm until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he bends his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm with the displaced finger.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 Because the joint is dislocated and will not return to its place, administer strong extension; have two people extend the arm and hold it with two hands so that it does not move during the extension, then bend the arm in both directions while holding a double-length and wide cloth; when the surgeon has put the joint in place with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns to its place; once it is in place, apply dry emplaster with egg yolk, and hold the arm tightly against the patient's neck, leaving it for several days before releasing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, loosen the binding and let it be; and if you see that the joint is not well aligned, repeat the ointment and binding, and leave it in this way for several days until it is securely set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels great pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe and rub him well, and press until he is relieved; or put sheep fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then replace the fat, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until it is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung warmed with butter, and bind it on; it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	hand dislocation
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated and returns easily, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be quickly returned to its place at once when it becomes dislocated, so that the place becomes swollen or a hot abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting is that you put the sick hand on a table, and stretch out the minister's hand, and the doctor places it evenly, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and presses until it returns to normal; but it is necessary for you to look if it is in place; then make the patient put the back of his hand on a table during the stretching and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and let the doctor put his hand on the aforementioned part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, that is good. If not, bind it with a plaster of soothing emplasters for abscesses and leave it like that without further intervention.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it and you are unable to set it in place after several days, let the joint remain dislocated; and it will not harm the patient as long as his hand remains moist and he is unable to clench anything at all. At that point, know that the nerves or arteries are cut, and there is no other remedy but to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps that will be of some help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they cannot move it well, and there is some cracking, wet it with warm water and rub it until it heals.[Read More](https://www.reddit.com/user/La-Baleine-Bleue/comments/v5169p/a_collection_of_translations_of_medieval/)
de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand dislocate on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then straighten the finger, and push the dislocation to its natural place until it returns, then hold the finger's head and pull it towards the side where it is disjointed; and leave it for 2 days, and then align it on that day; and tie it at night, as we have said, and untie it during the day, and make it move, and rebind it at night; and do this frequently, until it becomes tight, and similarly do if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and similarly do when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the loins of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the swelling of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death is imminent for the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that stools come out involuntarily, and he cannot hold them back, and often certain members become paralyzed, or both thighs or the two arms or one of them, and often the hips move in four ways; the one that moves backward is called "gilbositez": the cure is to check if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if it has, there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that comes from falling or being struck or similar things, the ancient methods of cures say with great solemnity, there is not much benefit in all cases; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have created instruments in diverse ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling that comes to the front of the breast, there is no engine or health; and also that which comes directly in two sides, and cannot be cured except by the one who comes properly from the back, as I say; and it is that the patient is stretched out on his face evenly, and has support beneath, so that he does not wound himself; then stick one stake firmly in the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a rope underneath the patient's ankles, and another around his calves, and knees, and ankles; and two assistants know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they are well tightened, the stakes as we have said, and the assistant places his palms on the spine very firmly, until it comes back to life.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board of three arms' length, and prop it up under the patient, and have the patient lie on their side, and place the head of the board under the affected area, then put the middle of the board on the patient's spine; and have the attendant place their feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do this with a device that is turned by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you drive two stakes into the patient's head, one of a large arm's length, and two others towards the feet; and have between each stake, below and above, a handspan of space; and have in each stake one hole, where the device turns, and have the stakes firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes have one turning stake, on which the ropes turn, and have two small stakes of a palm's length, to turn the device; and then tie the rope that is among the saddles to the device towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet at the other device, and each of the attendants turns their device to full tension, and the master sets the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is aligned, place a desiccative plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the compresses, and then an iron style of three fingers long, which reaches the area of the gelatinous tissue and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and let the patient use gentle exercise until it is healed; and if any problem arises at the end of the healing process, then laxative and soothing medicines should be administered, along with the iron style mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes there appears on the back shoulder blade, and one thinks it is dislocation; but it is the bone that is visible, therefore one must not make any assumptions: perhaps it could bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the hip joints and shoulder joints do not come out of place except for dislocations only, and they do not come out in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint comes out of place in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation is such that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears higher than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee by the fire; and the area that is swollen is warmed by an abscess because the hip comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this, when it comes to a lack, is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this, when it comes to the fore, is that he extends his leg in accordance with its completion; however, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot move forward, and he holds his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of this, when it comes afterward, is that he cannot stretch or bend his knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is relaxed, and the head of the femur is located near the lower part of the ribs.[ Italien](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Langue_italienne "Langue italienne")[Edit](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/italien#/media/Fichier:Flag_of_Italy.svg) **italien** (fém.)
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reduction of this type of dislocation is as follows: you should examine whether the dislocation is old and remains in its position, in which case there is no need for treatment, and one should not make any assumptions.[ Wiktionary ][edit](https://en.wiktionary.org/w/index.php?title=Wiktionary:Maintenance_template&action=edit) Maintenance template
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocations, hurry to turn the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare and strongly hold the leg with two hands, or with a ligament tied above the knee; and another minister extends their hand above in such a way that they push their hands beneath their heels, then tightly bind a soft ligament on the thigh; and another holds the end of the ligament; and they all stretch upwards and downwards at once, so that the sick person is lifted off the ground at once and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 Unless otherwise stated, when the dislocation is on the outside, one should attend to its likeness. When the dislocation is on the inside, you should turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place a bandage on the root of the thigh and the area beneath the groin. Next, stretch the bandage upwards towards the groin and hip; then have another assistant take hold of the patient's arms and embrace the affected thigh, stretching it outward strongly. This way, it will return to its place; and this type of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary to tie the patient's two feet together with a strong and soft ligament at the heels and knees, while keeping the affected leg stretched out two inches more than the other; then it should be hung from a beam above the head, and be suspended at least two arms' length from the ground. Command one assistant to embrace the thigh of the patient, while another assistant, who is also hanging with the patient, forcefully embraces the thigh, for the joint will quickly return to its place.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the case of gout, and tighten the ligament on the sick leg properly, and likewise on the pelvis; then place two sticks, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one stick between the thighs of the patient in the middle; and have a damp cloth placed around to prevent injury, then each assistant stretches out towards him, and the surgeon places his hand evenly on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns (the dislocation), that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place them on a table and press as we have said in the case of gout, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to quickly stretch out the sick leg as I have said; and let the doctor take the effort to be over the angular part of the limb, then press with the other hand and stretch it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is outwards, one should not stretch the patient downwards, nor lift them up, but they should be in the same position as if the hip was dislocated outwards, as we have said about lying on two hips; and be on their back, and the bandages extended as we have said before, and pressure should be applied to the joint on the table; and it will be sufficient when the patient stretches their legs and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and apply the plaster, and the strain of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then loosen, and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, strain as before, and leave for three days; then loosen, and make them walk gently, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee dislocates in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; but never forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it doesn't reach his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull it out between your hands, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee; and another minister extends his foot, so that the knee comes back to its place, and the sign is that he can easily bend his leg to his thigh; and apply the dressing on it, and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then unbind it; and the patient does not exert himself to go, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not in a good position, extend it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of a dislocated ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated, and at other times fully dislocated, both internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it protrudes at the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it moves slightly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright, and hold them by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards and place the foot nicely upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, by pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, start the work again, because it will return; and if it cannot return like this, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloth around so as not to hurt the patient; then hold the thigh with one assistant, and another assistant extend the good leg with their hands or a strap, tying it above the shin; then each assistant should pull evenly, and the stake should be firmly between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when stretched; then the doctor should place the dislocation in their hands, and another assistant should hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the bandage loosens, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for 4 days; and if they go before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, you must calm them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.[Comment: "calm" is used here to translate "apaiser", which can mean "to calm," but also "to soothe," or "to relieve." I chose "calm" because it fits well with the image of abscesses being soothed or relieved. In a modern medical context, the equivalent would be draining or lancing an abscess to remove pus and promote healing.]
des dois	thumbs[Comment: "des dois" is the genitive plural form of "le doy", meaning "the thumb". So "des dois" means "of the thumbs".]
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two ( bones) are dislocated, they should be smoothly stretched without effort, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any joint of the ankle, you should make the patient sit upright on a level surface or table, and place your foot on what is visible of those joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns to its proper place; and when it is aligned and there is nothing apparent, place a two-chambered board under the sole of the foot, then bind it firmly and leave it for 3 days, then untie it; and let it rest until it has healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	(about) wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often times the patient dies; so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it long, and if you are not pitying and merciful and slow, not hasty; and use at the beginning soothing remedies for the inflamed abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the inflamed abscess may come there; and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing remedies for the inflamed abscess, and treat the wound as it is appropriate, with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are dislocated, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your art and your body.
Amen	 Amen
